<p class="line" name=1.10.13>Hath not that honour in't it had; for where</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.14>I thought to crush him in an equal force,</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.15>True sword to sword, I'll potch at him some way</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.16>Or wrath or craft may get him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=1.10.17>He's the devil.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=1.10.18>Bolder, though not so subtle. My valour's poison'd</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.19>With only suffering stain by him; for him</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.20>Shall fly out of itself: nor sleep nor sanctuary,</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.21>Being naked, sick, nor fane nor Capitol,</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.22>The prayers of priests nor times of sacrifice,</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.23>Embarquements all of fury, shall lift up</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.24>Their rotten privilege and custom 'gainst</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.25>My hate to Marcius: where I find him, were it</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.26>At home, upon my brother's guard, even there,</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.27>Against the hospitable canon, would I</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.28>Wash my fierce hand in's heart. Go you to the city;</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.29>Learn how 'tis held; and what they are that must</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.30>Be hostages for Rome.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=1.10.31>Will not you go?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=1.10.32>I am attended at the cypress grove: I pray you--</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.33>'Tis south the city mills--bring me word thither</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.34>How the world goes, that to the pace of it</p>
<p class="line" name=1.10.35>I may spur on my journey.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>First Soldier</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=1.10.36>I shall, sir.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote><p>
<H3>ACT II</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. Rome. A public place.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter MENENIUS with the two Tribunes of the people, SICINIUS and BRUTUS.</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.1>The augurer tells me we shall have news to-night.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.2>Good or bad?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.3>Not according to the prayer of the people, for they</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.4>love not Marcius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.5>Nature teaches beasts to know their friends.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.6>Pray you, who does the wolf love?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.7>The lamb.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.8>Ay, to devour him; as the hungry plebeians would the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.9>noble Marcius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.10>He's a lamb indeed, that baes like a bear.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.11>He's a bear indeed, that lives like a lamb. You two</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.12>are old men: tell me one thing that I shall ask you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Both</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.13>Well, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.14>In what enormity is Marcius poor in, that you two</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.15>have not in abundance?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.16>He's poor in no one fault, but stored with all.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.17>Especially in pride.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.18>And topping all others in boasting.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.19>This is strange now: do you two know how you are</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.20>censured here in the city, I mean of us o' the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.21>right-hand file? do you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>Both</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.22>Why, how are we censured?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.23>Because you talk of pride now,--will you not be angry?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>Both</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.24>Well, well, sir, well.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.25>Why, 'tis no great matter; for a very little thief of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.26>occasion will rob you of a great deal of patience:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.27>give your dispositions the reins, and be angry at</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.28>your pleasures; at the least if you take it as a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.29>pleasure to you in being so. You blame Marcius for</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.30>being proud?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.31>We do it not alone, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.32>I know you can do very little alone; for your helps</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.33>are many, or else your actions would grow wondrous</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.34>single: your abilities are too infant-like for</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.35>doing much alone. You talk of pride: O that you</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.36>could turn your eyes toward the napes of your necks,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.37>and make but an interior survey of your good selves!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.38>O that you could!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.39>What then, sir?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.40>Why, then you should discover a brace of unmeriting,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.41>proud, violent, testy magistrates, alias fools, as</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.42>any in Rome.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.43>Menenius, you are known well enough too.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.44>I am known to be a humorous patrician, and one that</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.45>loves a cup of hot wine with not a drop of allaying</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.46>Tiber in't; said to be something imperfect in</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.47>favouring the first complaint; hasty and tinder-like</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.48>upon too trivial motion; one that converses more</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.49>with the buttock of the night than with the forehead</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.50>of the morning: what I think I utter, and spend my</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.51>malice in my breath. Meeting two such wealsmen as</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.52>you are--I cannot call you Lycurguses--if the drink</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.53>you give me touch my palate adversely, I make a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.54>crooked face at it. I can't say your worships have</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.55>delivered the matter well, when I find the ass in</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.56>compound with the major part of your syllables: and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.57>though I must be content to bear with those that say</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.58>you are reverend grave men, yet they lie deadly that</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.59>tell you you have good faces. If you see this in</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.60>the map of my microcosm, follows it that I am known</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.61>well enough too? what barm can your bisson</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.62>conspectuities glean out of this character, if I be</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.63>known well enough too?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.64>Come, sir, come, we know you well enough.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.65>You know neither me, yourselves nor any thing. You</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.66>are ambitious for poor knaves' caps and legs: you</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.67>wear out a good wholesome forenoon in hearing a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.68>cause between an orange wife and a fosset-seller;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.69>and then rejourn the controversy of three pence to a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.70>second day of audience. When you are hearing a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.71>matter between party and party, if you chance to be</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.72>pinched with the colic, you make faces like</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.73>mummers; set up the bloody flag against all</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.74>patience; and, in roaring for a chamber-pot,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.75>dismiss the controversy bleeding the more entangled</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.76>by your hearing: all the peace you make in their</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.77>cause is, calling both the parties knaves. You are</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.78>a pair of strange ones.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.79>Come, come, you are well understood to be a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.80>perfecter giber for the table than a necessary</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.81>bencher in the Capitol.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.82>Our very priests must become mockers, if they shall</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.83>encounter such ridiculous subjects as you are. When</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.84>you speak best unto the purpose, it is not worth the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.85>wagging of your beards; and your beards deserve not</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.86>so honourable a grave as to stuff a botcher's</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.87>cushion, or to be entombed in an ass's pack-</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.88>saddle. Yet you must be saying, Marcius is proud;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.89>who in a cheap estimation, is worth predecessors</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.90>since Deucalion, though peradventure some of the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.91>best of 'em were hereditary hangmen. God-den to</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.92>your worships: more of your conversation would</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.93>infect my brain, being the herdsmen of the beastly</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.94>plebeians: I will be bold to take my leave of you.</p>
<p><i>BRUTUS and SICINIUS go aside</i></p>
<p><i>Enter VOLUMNIA, VIRGILIA, and VALERIA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.95>How now, my as fair as noble ladies,--and the moon,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.96>were she earthly, no nobler,--whither do you follow</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.97>your eyes so fast?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.98>Honourable Menenius, my boy Marcius approaches; for</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.99>the love of Juno, let's go.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.100>Ha! Marcius coming home!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.101>Ay, worthy Menenius; and with most prosperous</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.102>approbation.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.103>Take my cap, Jupiter, and I thank thee. Hoo!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.104>Marcius coming home!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>VIRGILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.105>Nay,'tis true.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.106>Look, here's a letter from him: the state hath</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.107>another, his wife another; and, I think, there's one</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.108>at home for you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.109>I will make my very house reel tonight: a letter for</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.110>me!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>VIRGILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.111>Yes, certain, there's a letter for you; I saw't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.112>A letter for me! it gives me an estate of seven</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.113>years' health; in which time I will make a lip at</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.114>the physician: the most sovereign prescription in</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.115>Galen is but empiricutic, and, to this preservative,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.116>of no better report than a horse-drench. Is he</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.117>not wounded? he was wont to come home wounded.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>VIRGILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.118>O, no, no, no.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.119>O, he is wounded; I thank the gods for't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.120>So do I too, if it be not too much: brings a'</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.121>victory in his pocket? the wounds become him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.122>On's brows: Menenius, he comes the third time home</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.123>with the oaken garland.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.124>Has he disciplined Aufidius soundly?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.125>Titus Lartius writes, they fought together, but</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.126>Aufidius got off.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.127>And 'twas time for him too, I'll warrant him that:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.128>an he had stayed by him, I would not have been so</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.129>fidiused for all the chests in Corioli, and the gold</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.130>that's in them. Is the senate possessed of this?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.131>Good ladies, let's go. Yes, yes, yes; the senate</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.132>has letters from the general, wherein he gives my</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.133>son the whole name of the war: he hath in this</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.134>action outdone his former deeds doubly</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>VALERIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.135>In troth, there's wondrous things spoke of him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.136>Wondrous! ay, I warrant you, and not without his</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.137>true purchasing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>VIRGILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.138>The gods grant them true!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.139>True! pow, wow.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.140>True! I'll be sworn they are true.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.141>Where is he wounded?</p>
<p><i>To the Tribunes</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.142>God save your good worships! Marcius is coming</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.143>home: he has more cause to be proud. Where is he wounded?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.144>I' the shoulder and i' the left arm there will be</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.145>large cicatrices to show the people, when he shall</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.146>stand for his place. He received in the repulse of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.147>Tarquin seven hurts i' the body.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.148>One i' the neck, and two i' the thigh,--there's</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.149>nine that I know.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.150>He had, before this last expedition, twenty-five</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.151>wounds upon him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.152>Now it's twenty-seven: every gash was an enemy's grave.</p>
<p><i>A shout and flourish</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.153>Hark! the trumpets.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.154>These are the ushers of Marcius: before him he</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.155>carries noise, and behind him he leaves tears:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.156>Death, that dark spirit, in 's nervy arm doth lie;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.157>Which, being advanced, declines, and then men die.</p>
<p><i>A sennet. Trumpets sound. Enter COMINIUS the  general, and TITUS LARTIUS; between them, CORIOLANUS,  crowned with an oaken garland; with Captains and Soldiers, and a Herald</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>Herald</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.158>Know, Rome, that all alone Marcius did fight</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.159>Within Corioli gates: where he hath won,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.160>With fame, a name to Caius Marcius; these</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.161>In honour follows Coriolanus.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.162>Welcome to Rome, renowned Coriolanus!</p>
<p><i>Flourish</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.163>Welcome to Rome, renowned Coriolanus!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.164>No more of this; it does offend my heart:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.165>Pray now, no more.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.166>                  Look, sir, your mother!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.167>O,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.168>You have, I know, petition'd all the gods</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.169>For my prosperity!</p>
<p><i>Kneels</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.170>                  Nay, my good soldier, up;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.171>My gentle Marcius, worthy Caius, and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.172>By deed-achieving honour newly named,--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.173>What is it?--Coriolanus must I call thee?--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.174>But O, thy wife!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.175>                  My gracious silence, hail!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.176>Wouldst thou have laugh'd had I come coffin'd home,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.177>That weep'st to see me triumph? Ay, my dear,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.178>Such eyes the widows in Corioli wear,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.179>And mothers that lack sons.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.180>Now, the gods crown thee!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.181>And live you yet?</p>
<p><i>To VALERIA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.182>O my sweet lady, pardon.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.183>I know not where to turn: O, welcome home:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.184>And welcome, general: and ye're welcome all.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.185>A hundred thousand welcomes. I could weep</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.186>And I could laugh, I am light and heavy. Welcome.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.187>A curse begin at very root on's heart,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.188>That is not glad to see thee! You are three</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.189>That Rome should dote on: yet, by the faith of men,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.190>We have some old crab-trees here</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.191>at home that will not</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.192>Be grafted to your relish. Yet welcome, warriors:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.193>We call a nettle but a nettle and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.194>The faults of fools but folly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.195>Ever right.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.196>Menenius ever, ever.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>Herald</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.197>Give way there, and go on!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.198>[To VOLUMNIA and VIRGILIA]  Your hand, and yours:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.199>Ere in our own house I do shade my head,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.200>The good patricians must be visited;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.201>From whom I have received not only greetings,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.202>But with them change of honours.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.203>I have lived</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.204>To see inherited my very wishes</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.205>And the buildings of my fancy: only</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.206>There's one thing wanting, which I doubt not but</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.207>Our Rome will cast upon thee.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.208>Know, good mother,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.209>I had rather be their servant in my way,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.210>Than sway with them in theirs.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech75><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.211>On, to the Capitol!</p>
<p><i>Flourish. Cornets. Exeunt in state, as before. BRUTUS and SICINIUS come forward</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech76><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.212>All tongues speak of him, and the bleared sights</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.213>Are spectacled to see him: your prattling nurse</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.214>Into a rapture lets her baby cry</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.215>While she chats him: the kitchen malkin pins</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.216>Her richest lockram 'bout her reechy neck,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.217>Clambering the walls to eye him: stalls, bulks, windows,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.218>Are smother'd up, leads fill'd, and ridges horsed</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.219>With variable complexions, all agreeing</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.220>In earnestness to see him: seld-shown flamens</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.221>Do press among the popular throngs and puff</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.222>To win a vulgar station: or veil'd dames</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.223>Commit the war of white and damask in</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.224>Their nicely-gawded cheeks to the wanton spoil</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.225>Of Phoebus' burning kisses: such a pother</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.226>As if that whatsoever god who leads him</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.227>Were slily crept into his human powers</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.228>And gave him graceful posture.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech77><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.229>On the sudden,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.230>I warrant him consul.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech78><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.231>Then our office may,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.232>During his power, go sleep.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech79><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.233>He cannot temperately transport his honours</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.234>From where he should begin and end, but will</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.235>Lose those he hath won.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech80><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.236>In that there's comfort.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech81><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.237>Doubt not</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.238>The commoners, for whom we stand, but they</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.239>Upon their ancient malice will forget</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.240>With the least cause these his new honours, which</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.241>That he will give them make I as little question</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.242>As he is proud to do't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech82><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.243>I heard him swear,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.244>Were he to stand for consul, never would he</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.245>Appear i' the market-place nor on him put</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.246>The napless vesture of humility;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.247>Nor showing, as the manner is, his wounds</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.248>To the people, beg their stinking breaths.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech83><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.249>'Tis right.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech84><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.250>It was his word: O, he would miss it rather</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.251>Than carry it but by the suit of the gentry to him,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.252>And the desire of the nobles.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech85><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.253>I wish no better</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.254>Than have him hold that purpose and to put it</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.255>In execution.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech86><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.256>'Tis most like he will.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech87><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.257>It shall be to him then as our good wills,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.258>A sure destruction.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech88><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.259>So it must fall out</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.260>To him or our authorities. For an end,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.261>We must suggest the people in what hatred</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.262>He still hath held them; that to's power he would</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.263>Have made them mules, silenced their pleaders and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.264>Dispropertied their freedoms, holding them,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.265>In human action and capacity,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.266>Of no more soul nor fitness for the world</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.267>Than camels in the war, who have their provand</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.268>Only for bearing burdens, and sore blows</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.269>For sinking under them.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech89><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.270>This, as you say, suggested</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.271>At some time when his soaring insolence</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.272>Shall touch the people--which time shall not want,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.273>If he be put upon 't; and that's as easy</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.274>As to set dogs on sheep--will be his fire</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.275>To kindle their dry stubble; and their blaze</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.276>Shall darken him for ever.</p>
<p><i>Enter a Messenger</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech90><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.277>What's the matter?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech91><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.278>You are sent for to the Capitol. 'Tis thought</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.279>That Marcius shall be consul:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.280>I have seen the dumb men throng to see him and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.281>The blind to bear him speak: matrons flung gloves,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.282>Ladies and maids their scarfs and handkerchers,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.283>Upon him as he pass'd: the nobles bended,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.284>As to Jove's statue, and the commons made</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.285>A shower and thunder with their caps and shouts:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.286>I never saw the like.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech92><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.287>Let's to the Capitol;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.288>And carry with us ears and eyes for the time,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.289>But hearts for the event.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech93><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.290>Have with you.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. The same. The Capitol.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter two Officers, to lay cushions</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>First Officer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.1>Come, come, they are almost here. How many stand</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.2>for consulships?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Second Officer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.3>Three, they say: but 'tis thought of every one</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.4>Coriolanus will carry it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>First Officer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.5>That's a brave fellow; but he's vengeance proud, and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.6>loves not the common people.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Second Officer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.7>Faith, there had been many great men that have</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.8>flattered the people, who ne'er loved them; and there</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.9>be many that they have loved, they know not</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.10>wherefore: so that, if they love they know not why,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.11>they hate upon no better a ground: therefore, for</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.12>Coriolanus neither to care whether they love or hate</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.13>him manifests the true knowledge he has in their</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.14>disposition; and out of his noble carelessness lets</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.15>them plainly see't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>First Officer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.16>If he did not care whether he had their love or no,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.17>he waved indifferently 'twixt doing them neither</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.18>good nor harm: but he seeks their hate with greater</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.19>devotion than can render it him; and leaves</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.20>nothing undone that may fully discover him their</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.21>opposite. Now, to seem to affect the malice and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.22>displeasure of the people is as bad as that which he</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.23>dislikes, to flatter them for their love.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Second Officer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.24>He hath deserved worthily of his country: and his</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.25>ascent is not by such easy degrees as those who,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.26>having been supple and courteous to the people,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.27>bonneted, without any further deed to have them at</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.28>an into their estimation and report: but he hath so</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.29>planted his honours in their eyes, and his actions</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.30>in their hearts, that for their tongues to be</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.31>silent, and not confess so much, were a kind of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.32>ingrateful injury; to report otherwise, were a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.33>malice, that, giving itself the lie, would pluck</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.34>reproof and rebuke from every ear that heard it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>First Officer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.35>No more of him; he is a worthy man: make way, they</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.36>are coming.</p>
<p><i>A sennet. Enter, with actors before them, COMINIUS  the consul, MENENIUS, CORIOLANUS, Senators,  SICINIUS and BRUTUS. The Senators take their  places; the Tribunes take their Places by themselves. CORIOLANUS stands</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.37>Having determined of the Volsces and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.38>To send for Titus Lartius, it remains,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.39>As the main point of this our after-meeting,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.40>To gratify his noble service that</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.41>Hath thus stood for his country: therefore,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.42>please you,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.43>Most reverend and grave elders, to desire</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.44>The present consul, and last general</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.45>In our well-found successes, to report</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.46>A little of that worthy work perform'd</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.47>By Caius Marcius Coriolanus, whom</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.48>We met here both to thank and to remember</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.49>With honours like himself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.50>Speak, good Cominius:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.51>Leave nothing out for length, and make us think</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.52>Rather our state's defective for requital</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.53>Than we to stretch it out.</p>
<p><i>To the Tribunes</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.54>Masters o' the people,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.55>We do request your kindest ears, and after,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.56>Your loving motion toward the common body,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.57>To yield what passes here.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.58>We are convented</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.59>Upon a pleasing treaty, and have hearts</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.60>Inclinable to honour and advance</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.61>The theme of our assembly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.62>Which the rather</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.63>We shall be blest to do, if he remember</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.64>A kinder value of the people than</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.65>He hath hereto prized them at.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.66>That's off, that's off;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.67>I would you rather had been silent. Please you</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.68>To hear Cominius speak?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.69>Most willingly;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.70>But yet my caution was more pertinent</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.71>Than the rebuke you give it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.72>He loves your people</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.73>But tie him not to be their bedfellow.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.74>Worthy Cominius, speak.</p>
<p><i>CORIOLANUS offers to go away</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.75>Nay, keep your place.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.76>Sit, Coriolanus; never shame to hear</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.77>What you have nobly done.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.78>Your horror's pardon:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.79>I had rather have my wounds to heal again</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.80>Than hear say how I got them.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.81>Sir, I hope</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.82>My words disbench'd you not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.83>No, sir: yet oft,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.84>When blows have made me stay, I fled from words.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.85>You soothed not, therefore hurt not: but</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.86>your people,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.87>I love them as they weigh.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.88>Pray now, sit down.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.89>I had rather have one scratch my head i' the sun</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.90>When the alarum were struck than idly sit</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.91>To hear my nothings monster'd.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.92>Masters of the people,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.93>Your multiplying spawn how can he flatter--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.94>That's thousand to one good one--when you now see</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.95>He had rather venture all his limbs for honour</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.96>Than one on's ears to hear it? Proceed, Cominius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.97>I shall lack voice: the deeds of Coriolanus</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.98>Should not be utter'd feebly. It is held</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.99>That valour is the chiefest virtue, and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.100>Most dignifies the haver: if it be,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.101>The man I speak of cannot in the world</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.102>Be singly counterpoised. At sixteen years,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.103>When Tarquin made a head for Rome, he fought</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.104>Beyond the mark of others: our then dictator,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.105>Whom with all praise I point at, saw him fight,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.106>When with his Amazonian chin he drove</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.107>The bristled lips before him: be bestrid</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.108>An o'er-press'd Roman and i' the consul's view</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.109>Slew three opposers: Tarquin's self he met,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.110>And struck him on his knee: in that day's feats,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.111>When he might act the woman in the scene,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.112>He proved best man i' the field, and for his meed</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.113>Was brow-bound with the oak. His pupil age</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.114>Man-enter'd thus, he waxed like a sea,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.115>And in the brunt of seventeen battles since</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.116>He lurch'd all swords of the garland. For this last,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.117>Before and in Corioli, let me say,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.118>I cannot speak him home: he stopp'd the fliers;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.119>And by his rare example made the coward</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.120>Turn terror into sport: as weeds before</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.121>A vessel under sail, so men obey'd</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.122>And fell below his stem: his sword, death's stamp,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.123>Where it did mark, it took; from face to foot</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.124>He was a thing of blood, whose every motion</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.125>Was timed with dying cries: alone he enter'd</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.126>The mortal gate of the city, which he painted</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.127>With shunless destiny; aidless came off,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.128>And with a sudden reinforcement struck</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.129>Corioli like a planet: now all's his:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.130>When, by and by, the din of war gan pierce</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.131>His ready sense; then straight his doubled spirit</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.132>Re-quicken'd what in flesh was fatigate,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.133>And to the battle came he; where he did</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.134>Run reeking o'er the lives of men, as if</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.135>'Twere a perpetual spoil: and till we call'd</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.136>Both field and city ours, he never stood</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.137>To ease his breast with panting.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.138>Worthy man!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.139>He cannot but with measure fit the honours</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.140>Which we devise him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.141>Our spoils he kick'd at,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.142>And look'd upon things precious as they were</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.143>The common muck of the world: he covets less</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.144>Than misery itself would give; rewards</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.145>His deeds with doing them, and is content</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.146>To spend the time to end it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.147>He's right noble:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.148>Let him be call'd for.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.149>Call Coriolanus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>Officer</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.150>He doth appear.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter CORIOLANUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.151>The senate, Coriolanus, are well pleased</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.152>To make thee consul.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.153>I do owe them still</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.154>My life and services.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.155>It then remains</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.156>That you do speak to the people.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.157>I do beseech you,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.158>Let me o'erleap that custom, for I cannot</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.159>Put on the gown, stand naked and entreat them,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.160>For my wounds' sake, to give their suffrage: please you</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.161>That I may pass this doing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.162>Sir, the people</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.163>Must have their voices; neither will they bate</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.164>One jot of ceremony.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.165>Put them not to't:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.166>Pray you, go fit you to the custom and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.167>Take to you, as your predecessors have,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.168>Your honour with your form.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.169>It is apart</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.170>That I shall blush in acting, and might well</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.171>Be taken from the people.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.172>Mark you that?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.173>To brag unto them, thus I did, and thus;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.174>Show them the unaching scars which I should hide,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.175>As if I had received them for the hire</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.176>Of their breath only!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.177>Do not stand upon't.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.178>We recommend to you, tribunes of the people,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.179>Our purpose to them: and to our noble consul</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.180>Wish we all joy and honour.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>Senators</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.181>To Coriolanus come all joy and honour!</p>
<p><i>Flourish of cornets. Exeunt all but SICINIUS and BRUTUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.182>You see how he intends to use the people.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.183>May they perceive's intent! He will require them,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.184>As if he did contemn what he requested</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.185>Should be in them to give.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.186>Come, we'll inform them</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.187>Of our proceedings here: on the marketplace,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.188>I know, they do attend us.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. The same. The Forum.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter seven or eight Citizens</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.1>Once, if he do require our voices, we ought not to deny him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.2>We may, sir, if we will.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.3>We have power in ourselves to do it, but it is a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.4>power that we have no power to do; for if he show us</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.5>his wounds and tell us his deeds, we are to put our</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.6>tongues into those wounds and speak for them; so, if</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.7>he tell us his noble deeds, we must also tell him</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.8>our noble acceptance of them. Ingratitude is</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.9>monstrous, and for the multitude to be ingrateful,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.10>were to make a monster of the multitude: of the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.11>which we being members, should bring ourselves to be</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.12>monstrous members.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.13>And to make us no better thought of, a little help</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.14>will serve; for once we stood up about the corn, he</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.15>himself stuck not to call us the many-headed multitude.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.16>We have been called so of many; not that our heads</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.17>are some brown, some black, some auburn, some bald,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.18>but that our wits are so diversely coloured: and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.19>truly I think if all our wits were to issue out of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.20>one skull, they would fly east, west, north, south,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.21>and their consent of one direct way should be at</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.22>once to all the points o' the compass.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.23>Think you so? Which way do you judge my wit would</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.24>fly?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.25>Nay, your wit will not so soon out as another man's</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.26>will;'tis strongly wedged up in a block-head, but</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.27>if it were at liberty, 'twould, sure, southward.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.28>Why that way?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.29>To lose itself in a fog, where being three parts</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.30>melted away with rotten dews, the fourth would return</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.31>for conscience sake, to help to get thee a wife.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.32>You are never without your tricks: you may, you may.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.33>Are you all resolved to give your voices? But</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.34>that's no matter, the greater part carries it. I</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.35>say, if he would incline to the people, there was</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.36>never a worthier man.</p>
<p><i>Enter CORIOLANUS in a gown of humility, with MENENIUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.37>Here he comes, and in the gown of humility: mark his</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.38>behavior. We are not to stay all together, but to</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.39>come by him where he stands, by ones, by twos, and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.40>by threes. He's to make his requests by</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.41>particulars; wherein every one of us has a single</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.42>honour, in giving him our own voices with our own</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.43>tongues: therefore follow me, and I direct you how</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.44>you shall go by him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.45>Content, content.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt Citizens</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.46>O sir, you are not right: have you not known</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.47>The worthiest men have done't?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.48>What must I say?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.49>'I Pray, sir'--Plague upon't! I cannot bring</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.50>My tongue to such a pace:--'Look, sir, my wounds!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.51>I got them in my country's service, when</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.52>Some certain of your brethren roar'd and ran</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.53>From the noise of our own drums.'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.54>O me, the gods!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.55>You must not speak of that: you must desire them</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.56>To think upon you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.57>                  Think upon me! hang 'em!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.58>I would they would forget me, like the virtues</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.59>Which our divines lose by 'em.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.60>You'll mar all:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.61>I'll leave you: pray you, speak to 'em, I pray you,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.62>In wholesome manner.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.63>Bid them wash their faces</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.64>And keep their teeth clean.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter two of the Citizens</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.65>So, here comes a brace.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter a third Citizen</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.66>You know the cause, air, of my standing here.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.67>We do, sir; tell us what hath brought you to't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.68>Mine own desert.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.69>Your own desert!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.70>Ay, but not mine own desire.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.71>How not your own desire?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.72>No, sir,'twas never my desire yet to trouble the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.73>poor with begging.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.74>You must think, if we give you any thing, we hope to</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.75>gain by you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.76>Well then, I pray, your price o' the consulship?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.77>The price is to ask it kindly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.78>Kindly! Sir, I pray, let me ha't: I have wounds to</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.79>show you, which shall be yours in private. Your</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.80>good voice, sir; what say you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.81>You shall ha' it, worthy sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.82>A match, sir. There's in all two worthy voices</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.83>begged. I have your alms: adieu.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.84>But this is something odd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.85>An 'twere to give again,--but 'tis no matter.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt the three Citizens</i></p>
<p><i>Re-enter two other Citizens</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.86>Pray you now, if it may stand with the tune of your</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.87>voices that I may be consul, I have here the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.88>customary gown.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.89>You have deserved nobly of your country, and you</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.90>have not deserved nobly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.91>Your enigma?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.92>You have been a scourge to her enemies, you have</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.93>been a rod to her friends; you have not indeed loved</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.94>the common people.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.95>You should account me the more virtuous that I have</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.96>not been common in my love. I will, sir, flatter my</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.97>sworn brother, the people, to earn a dearer</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.98>estimation of them; 'tis a condition they account</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.99>gentle: and since the wisdom of their choice is</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.100>rather to have my hat than my heart, I will practise</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.101>the insinuating nod and be off to them most</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.102>counterfeitly; that is, sir, I will counterfeit the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.103>bewitchment of some popular man and give it</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.104>bountiful to the desirers. Therefore, beseech you,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.105>I may be consul.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>Fifth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.106>We hope to find you our friend; and therefore give</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.107>you our voices heartily.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>Fourth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.108>You have received many wounds for your country.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.109>I will not seal your knowledge with showing them. I</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.110>will make much of your voices, and so trouble you no further.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>Both Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.111>The gods give you joy, sir, heartily!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.112>Most sweet voices!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.113>Better it is to die, better to starve,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.114>Than crave the hire which first we do deserve.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.115>Why in this woolvish toge should I stand here,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.116>To beg of Hob and Dick, that do appear,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.117>Their needless vouches? Custom calls me to't:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.118>What custom wills, in all things should we do't,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.119>The dust on antique time would lie unswept,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.120>And mountainous error be too highly heapt</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.121>For truth to o'er-peer. Rather than fool it so,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.122>Let the high office and the honour go</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.123>To one that would do thus. I am half through;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.124>The one part suffer'd, the other will I do.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter three Citizens more</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.125>Here come more voices.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.126>Your voices: for your voices I have fought;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.127>Watch'd for your voices; for Your voices bear</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.128>Of wounds two dozen odd; battles thrice six</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.129>I have seen and heard of; for your voices have</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.130>Done many things, some less, some more your voices:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.131>Indeed I would be consul.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>Sixth Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.132>He has done nobly, and cannot go without any honest</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.133>man's voice.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>Seventh Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.134>Therefore let him be consul: the gods give him joy,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.135>and make him good friend to the people!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>All Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.136>Amen, amen. God save thee, noble consul!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.137>Worthy voices!</p>
<p><i>Re-enter MENENIUS, with BRUTUS and SICINIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.138>You have stood your limitation; and the tribunes</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.139>Endue you with the people's voice: remains</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.140>That, in the official marks invested, you</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.141>Anon do meet the senate.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.142>Is this done?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.143>The custom of request you have discharged:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.144>The people do admit you, and are summon'd</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.145>To meet anon, upon your approbation.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.146>Where? at the senate-house?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.147>There, Coriolanus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.148>May I change these garments?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.149>You may, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.150>That I'll straight do; and, knowing myself again,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.151>Repair to the senate-house.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.152>I'll keep you company. Will you along?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.153>We stay here for the people.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.154>Fare you well.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt CORIOLANUS and MENENIUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.155>He has it now, and by his looks methink</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.156>'Tis warm at 's heart.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.157>With a proud heart he wore his humble weeds.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.158>will you dismiss the people?</p>
<p><i>Re-enter Citizens</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.159>How now, my masters! have you chose this man?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.160>He has our voices, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.161>We pray the gods he may deserve your loves.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.162>Amen, sir: to my poor unworthy notice,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.163>He mock'd us when he begg'd our voices.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.164>Certainly</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.165>He flouted us downright.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.166>No,'tis his kind of speech: he did not mock us.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.167>Not one amongst us, save yourself, but says</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.168>He used us scornfully: he should have show'd us</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.169>His marks of merit, wounds received for's country.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.170>Why, so he did, I am sure.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.171>No, no; no man saw 'em.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.172>He said he had wounds, which he could show</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.173>in private;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.174>And with his hat, thus waving it in scorn,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.175>'I would be consul,' says he: 'aged custom,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.176>But by your voices, will not so permit me;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.177>Your voices therefore.' When we granted that,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.178>Here was 'I thank you for your voices: thank you:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.179>Your most sweet voices: now you have left</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.180>your voices,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.181>I have no further with you.' Was not this mockery?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.182>Why either were you ignorant to see't,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.183>Or, seeing it, of such childish friendliness</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.184>To yield your voices?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.185>Could you not have told him</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.186>As you were lesson'd, when he had no power,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.187>But was a petty servant to the state,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.188>He was your enemy, ever spake against</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.189>Your liberties and the charters that you bear</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.190>I' the body of the weal; and now, arriving</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.191>A place of potency and sway o' the state,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.192>If he should still malignantly remain</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.193>Fast foe to the plebeii, your voices might</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.194>Be curses to yourselves? You should have said</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.195>That as his worthy deeds did claim no less</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.196>Than what he stood for, so his gracious nature</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.197>Would think upon you for your voices and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.198>Translate his malice towards you into love,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.199>Standing your friendly lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.200>Thus to have said,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.201>As you were fore-advised, had touch'd his spirit</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.202>And tried his inclination; from him pluck'd</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.203>Either his gracious promise, which you might,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.204>As cause had call'd you up, have held him to</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.205>Or else it would have gall'd his surly nature,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.206>Which easily endures not article</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.207>Tying him to aught; so putting him to rage,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.208>You should have ta'en the advantage of his choler</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.209>And pass'd him unelected.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.210>Did you perceive</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.211>He did solicit you in free contempt</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.212>When he did need your loves, and do you think</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.213>That his contempt shall not be bruising to you,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.214>When he hath power to crush? Why, had your bodies</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.215>No heart among you? or had you tongues to cry</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.216>Against the rectorship of judgment?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.217>Have you</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.218>Ere now denied the asker? and now again</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.219>Of him that did not ask, but mock, bestow</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.220>Your sued-for tongues?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.221>He's not confirm'd; we may deny him yet.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech75><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.222>And will deny him:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.223>I'll have five hundred voices of that sound.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech76><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.224>I twice five hundred and their friends to piece 'em.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech77><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.225>Get you hence instantly, and tell those friends,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.226>They have chose a consul that will from them take</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.227>Their liberties; make them of no more voice</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.228>Than dogs that are as often beat for barking</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.229>As therefore kept to do so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech78><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.230>Let them assemble,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.231>And on a safer judgment all revoke</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.232>Your ignorant election; enforce his pride,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.233>And his old hate unto you; besides, forget not</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.234>With what contempt he wore the humble weed,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.235>How in his suit he scorn'd you; but your loves,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.236>Thinking upon his services, took from you</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.237>The apprehension of his present portance,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.238>Which most gibingly, ungravely, he did fashion</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.239>After the inveterate hate he bears you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech79><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.240>Lay</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.241>A fault on us, your tribunes; that we laboured,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.242>No impediment between, but that you must</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.243>Cast your election on him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech80><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.244>Say, you chose him</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.245>More after our commandment than as guided</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.246>By your own true affections, and that your minds,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.247>Preoccupied with what you rather must do</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.248>Than what you should, made you against the grain</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.249>To voice him consul: lay the fault on us.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech81><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.250>Ay, spare us not. Say we read lectures to you.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.251>How youngly he began to serve his country,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.252>How long continued, and what stock he springs of,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.253>The noble house o' the Marcians, from whence came</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.254>That Ancus Marcius, Numa's daughter's son,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.255>Who, after great Hostilius, here was king;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.256>Of the same house Publius and Quintus were,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.257>That our beat water brought by conduits hither;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.258>And  [Censorinus,]  nobly named so,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.259>Twice being  [by the people chosen]  censor,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.260>Was his great ancestor.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech82><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.261>One thus descended,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.262>That hath beside well in his person wrought</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.263>To be set high in place, we did commend</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.264>To your remembrances: but you have found,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.265>Scaling his present bearing with his past,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.266>That he's your fixed enemy, and revoke</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.267>Your sudden approbation.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech83><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.268>Say, you ne'er had done't--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.269>Harp on that still--but by our putting on;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.270>And presently, when you have drawn your number,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.271>Repair to the Capitol.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech84><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.272>We will so: almost all</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.273>Repent in their election.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt Citizens</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech85><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.274>Let them go on;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.275>This mutiny were better put in hazard,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.276>Than stay, past doubt, for greater:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.277>If, as his nature is, he fall in rage</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.278>With their refusal, both observe and answer</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.279>The vantage of his anger.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech86><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.280>To the Capitol, come:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.281>We will be there before the stream o' the people;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.282>And this shall seem, as partly 'tis, their own,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.283>Which we have goaded onward.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote><p>
<H3>ACT III</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. Rome. A street.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Cornets. Enter CORIOLANUS, MENENIUS, all the Gentry, COMINIUS, TITUS LARTIUS, and other Senators</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.1>Tullus Aufidius then had made new head?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>LARTIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.2>He had, my lord; and that it was which caused</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.3>Our swifter composition.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.4>So then the Volsces stand but as at first,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.5>Ready, when time shall prompt them, to make road.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.6>Upon's again.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.7>They are worn, lord consul, so,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.8>That we shall hardly in our ages see</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.9>Their banners wave again.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.10>Saw you Aufidius?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>LARTIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.11>On safe-guard he  came to me; and did curse</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.12>Against the Volsces, for they had so vilely</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.13>Yielded the town: he is retired to Antium.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.14>Spoke he of me?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>LARTIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.15>                  He did, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.16>How? what?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>LARTIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.17>How often he had met you, sword to sword;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.18>That of all things upon the earth he hated</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.19>Your person most, that he would pawn his fortunes</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.20>To hopeless restitution, so he might</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.21>Be call'd your vanquisher.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.22>At Antium lives he?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>LARTIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.23>At Antium.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.24>I wish I had a cause to seek him there,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.25>To oppose his hatred fully. Welcome home.</p>
<p><i>Enter SICINIUS and BRUTUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.26>Behold, these are the tribunes of the people,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.27>The tongues o' the common mouth: I do despise them;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.28>For they do prank them in authority,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.29>Against all noble sufferance.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.30>Pass no further.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.31>Ha! what is that?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.32>It will be dangerous to go on: no further.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.33>What makes this change?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.34>The matter?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.35>Hath he not pass'd the noble and the common?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.36>Cominius, no.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.37>                  Have I had children's voices?</p>
</blockquote>
