<p class="line" name=speech22><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.38>Tribunes, give way; he shall to the market-place.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.39>The people are incensed against him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.40>Stop,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.41>Or all will fall in broil.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.42>Are these your herd?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.43>Must these have voices, that can yield them now</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.44>And straight disclaim their tongues? What are</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.45>your offices?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.46>You being their mouths, why rule you not their teeth?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.47>Have you not set them on?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.48>Be calm, be calm.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.49>It is a purposed thing, and grows by plot,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.50>To curb the will of the nobility:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.51>Suffer't, and live with such as cannot rule</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.52>Nor ever will be ruled.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.53>Call't not a plot:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.54>The people cry you mock'd them, and of late,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.55>When corn was given them gratis, you repined;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.56>Scandal'd the suppliants for the people, call'd them</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.57>Time-pleasers, flatterers, foes to nobleness.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.58>Why, this was known before.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.59>Not to them all.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.60>Have you inform'd them sithence?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.61>How! I inform them!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.62>You are like to do such business.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.63>Not unlike,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.64>Each way, to better yours.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.65>Why then should I be consul? By yond clouds,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.66>Let me deserve so ill as you, and make me</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.67>Your fellow tribune.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.68>You show too much of that</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.69>For which the people stir: if you will pass</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.70>To where you are bound, you must inquire your way,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.71>Which you are out of, with a gentler spirit,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.72>Or never be so noble as a consul,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.73>Nor yoke with him for tribune.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.74>Let's be calm.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.75>The people are abused; set on. This paltering</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.76>Becomes not Rome, nor has Coriolanus</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.77>Deserved this so dishonour'd rub, laid falsely</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.78>I' the plain way of his merit.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.79>Tell me of corn!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.80>This was my speech, and I will speak't again--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.81>Not now, not now.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.82>                  Not in this heat, sir, now.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.83>Now, as I live, I will. My nobler friends,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.84>I crave their pardons:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.85>For the mutable, rank-scented many, let them</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.86>Regard me as I do not flatter, and</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.87>Therein behold themselves: I say again,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.88>In soothing them, we nourish 'gainst our senate</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.89>The cockle of rebellion, insolence, sedition,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.90>Which we ourselves have plough'd for, sow'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.91>and scatter'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.92>By mingling them with us, the honour'd number,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.93>Who lack not virtue, no, nor power, but that</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.94>Which they have given to beggars.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.95>Well, no more.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.96>No more words, we beseech you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.97>How! no more!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.98>As for my country I have shed my blood,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.99>Not fearing outward force, so shall my lungs</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.100>Coin words till their decay against those measles,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.101>Which we disdain should tatter us, yet sought</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.102>The very way to catch them.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.103>You speak o' the people,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.104>As if you were a god to punish, not</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.105>A man of their infirmity.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.106>'Twere well</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.107>We let the people know't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.108>What, what? his choler?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.109>Choler!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.110>Were I as patient as the midnight sleep,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.111>By Jove, 'twould be my mind!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.112>It is a mind</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.113>That shall remain a poison where it is,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.114>Not poison any further.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.115>Shall remain!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.116>Hear you this Triton of the minnows? mark you</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.117>His absolute 'shall'?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.118>'Twas from the canon.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.119>'Shall'!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.120>O good but most unwise patricians! why,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.121>You grave but reckless senators, have you thus</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.122>Given Hydra here to choose an officer,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.123>That with his peremptory 'shall,' being but</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.124>The horn and noise o' the monster's, wants not spirit</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.125>To say he'll turn your current in a ditch,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.126>And make your channel his? If he have power</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.127>Then vail your ignorance; if none, awake</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.128>Your dangerous lenity. If you are learn'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.129>Be not as common fools; if you are not,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.130>Let them have cushions by you. You are plebeians,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.131>If they be senators: and they are no less,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.132>When, both your voices blended, the great'st taste</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.133>Most palates theirs. They choose their magistrate,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.134>And such a one as he, who puts his 'shall,'</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.135>His popular 'shall' against a graver bench</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.136>Than ever frown in Greece. By Jove himself!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.137>It makes the consuls base: and my soul aches</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.138>To know, when two authorities are up,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.139>Neither supreme, how soon confusion</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.140>May enter 'twixt the gap of both and take</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.141>The one by the other.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.142>Well, on to the market-place.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.143>Whoever gave that counsel, to give forth</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.144>The corn o' the storehouse gratis, as 'twas used</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.145>Sometime in Greece,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.146>Well, well, no more of that.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.147>Though there the people had more absolute power,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.148>I say, they nourish'd disobedience, fed</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.149>The ruin of the state.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.150>Why, shall the people give</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.151>One that speaks thus their voice?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.152>I'll give my reasons,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.153>More worthier than their voices. They know the corn</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.154>Was not our recompense, resting well assured</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.155>That ne'er did service for't: being press'd to the war,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.156>Even when the navel of the state was touch'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.157>They would not thread the gates. This kind of service</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.158>Did not deserve corn gratis. Being i' the war</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.159>Their mutinies and revolts, wherein they show'd</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.160>Most valour, spoke not for them: the accusation</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.161>Which they have often made against the senate,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.162>All cause unborn, could never be the motive</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.163>Of our so frank donation. Well, what then?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.164>How shall this bisson multitude digest</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.165>The senate's courtesy? Let deeds express</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.166>What's like to be their words: 'we did request it;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.167>We are the greater poll, and in true fear</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.168>They gave us our demands.' Thus we debase</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.169>The nature of our seats and make the rabble</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.170>Call our cares fears; which will in time</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.171>Break ope the locks o' the senate and bring in</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.172>The crows to peck the eagles.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.173>Come, enough.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.174>Enough, with over-measure.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.175>No, take more:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.176>What may be sworn by, both divine and human,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.177>Seal what I end withal! This double worship,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.178>Where one part does disdain with cause, the other</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.179>Insult without all reason, where gentry, title, wisdom,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.180>Cannot conclude but by the yea and no</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.181>Of general ignorance,--it must omit</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.182>Real necessities, and give way the while</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.183>To unstable slightness: purpose so barr'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.184>it follows,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.185>Nothing is done to purpose. Therefore, beseech you,--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.186>You that will be less fearful than discreet,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.187>That love the fundamental part of state</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.188>More than you doubt the change on't, that prefer</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.189>A noble life before a long, and wish</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.190>To jump a body with a dangerous physic</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.191>That's sure of death without it, at once pluck out</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.192>The multitudinous tongue; let them not lick</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.193>The sweet which is their poison: your dishonour</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.194>Mangles true judgment and bereaves the state</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.195>Of that integrity which should become't,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.196>Not having the power to do the good it would,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.197>For the in which doth control't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.198>Has said enough.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.199>Has spoken like a traitor, and shall answer</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.200>As traitors do.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.201>                  Thou wretch, despite o'erwhelm thee!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.202>What should the people do with these bald tribunes?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.203>On whom depending, their obedience fails</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.204>To the greater bench: in a rebellion,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.205>When what's not meet, but what must be, was law,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.206>Then were they chosen: in a better hour,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.207>Let what is meet be said it must be meet,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.208>And throw their power i' the dust.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.209>Manifest treason!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.210>                  This a consul? no.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.211>The aediles, ho!</p>
<p><i>Enter an AEdile</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.212>Let him be apprehended.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.213>Go, call the people:</p>
<p><i>Exit AEdile</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.214>in whose name myself</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.215>Attach thee as a traitorous innovator,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.216>A foe to the public weal: obey, I charge thee,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.217>And follow to thine answer.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.218>Hence, old goat!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.219>Senators,  & C	We'll surety him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.220>                  Aged sir, hands off.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.221>Hence, rotten thing! or I shall shake thy bones</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.222>Out of thy garments.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.223>Help, ye citizens!</p>
<p><i>Enter a rabble of Citizens (Plebeians), with the AEdiles</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.224>On both sides more respect.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech75><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.225>Here's he that would take from you all your power.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech76><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.226>Seize him, AEdiles!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech77><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.227>Down with him! down with him!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.228>Senators,  & C	Weapons, weapons, weapons!</p>
<p><i>They all bustle about CORIOLANUS, crying</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.229>'Tribunes!' 'Patricians!' 'Citizens!' 'What, ho!'</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.230>'Sicinius!' 'Brutus!' 'Coriolanus!' 'Citizens!'</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.231>'Peace, peace, peace!' 'Stay, hold, peace!'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech78><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.232>What is about to be? I am out of breath;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.233>Confusion's near; I cannot speak. You, tribunes</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.234>To the people! Coriolanus, patience!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.235>Speak, good Sicinius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech79><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.236>Hear me, people; peace!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech80><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.237>Let's hear our tribune: peace Speak, speak, speak.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech81><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.238>You are at point to lose your liberties:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.239>Marcius would have all from you; Marcius,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.240>Whom late you have named for consul.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech82><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.241>Fie, fie, fie!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.242>This is the way to kindle, not to quench.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech83><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.243>To unbuild the city and to lay all flat.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech84><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.244>What is the city but the people?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech85><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.245>True,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.246>The people are the city.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech86><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.247>By the consent of all, we were establish'd</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.248>The people's magistrates.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech87><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.249>You so remain.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech88><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.250>And so are like to do.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech89><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.251>That is the way to lay the city flat;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.252>To bring the roof to the foundation,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.253>And bury all, which yet distinctly ranges,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.254>In heaps and piles of ruin.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech90><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.255>This deserves death.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech91><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.256>Or let us stand to our authority,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.257>Or let us lose it. We do here pronounce,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.258>Upon the part o' the people, in whose power</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.259>We were elected theirs, Marcius is worthy</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.260>Of present death.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech92><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.261>                  Therefore lay hold of him;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.262>Bear him to the rock Tarpeian, and from thence</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.263>Into destruction cast him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech93><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.264>AEdiles, seize him!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech94><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.265>Yield, Marcius, yield!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech95><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.266>Hear me one word;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.267>Beseech you, tribunes, hear me but a word.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech96><b>AEdile</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.268>Peace, peace!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech97><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.269>[To BRUTUS]  Be that you seem, truly your</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.270>country's friend,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.271>And temperately proceed to what you would</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.272>Thus violently redress.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech98><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.273>Sir, those cold ways,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.274>That seem like prudent helps, are very poisonous</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.275>Where the disease is violent. Lay hands upon him,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.276>And bear him to the rock.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech99><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.277>No, I'll die here.</p>
<p><i>Drawing his sword</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.278>There's some among you have beheld me fighting:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.279>Come, try upon yourselves what you have seen me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech100><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.280>Down with that sword! Tribunes, withdraw awhile.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech101><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.281>Lay hands upon him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech102><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.282>Help Marcius, help,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.283>You that be noble; help him, young and old!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech103><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.284>Down with him, down with him!</p>
<p><i>In this mutiny, the Tribunes, the AEdiles, and the People, are beat in</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech104><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.285>Go, get you to your house; be gone, away!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.286>All will be naught else.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech105><b>Second Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.287>Get you gone.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech106><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.288>Stand fast;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.289>We have as many friends as enemies.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech107><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.290>Sham it be put to that?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech108><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.291>The gods forbid!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.292>I prithee, noble friend, home to thy house;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.293>Leave us to cure this cause.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech109><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.294>For 'tis a sore upon us,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.295>You cannot tent yourself: be gone, beseech you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech110><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.296>Come, sir, along with us.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech111><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.297>I would they were barbarians--as they are,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.298>Though in Rome litter'd--not Romans--as they are not,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.299>Though calved i' the porch o' the Capitol--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech112><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.300>Be gone;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.301>Put not your worthy rage into your tongue;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.302>One time will owe another.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech113><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.303>On fair ground</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.304>I could beat forty of them.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech114><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.305>I could myself</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.306>Take up a brace o' the best of them; yea, the</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.307>two tribunes:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.308>But now 'tis odds beyond arithmetic;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.309>And manhood is call'd foolery, when it stands</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.310>Against a falling fabric. Will you hence,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.311>Before the tag return? whose rage doth rend</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.312>Like interrupted waters and o'erbear</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.313>What they are used to bear.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech115><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.314>Pray you, be gone:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.315>I'll try whether my old wit be in request</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.316>With those that have but little: this must be patch'd</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.317>With cloth of any colour.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech116><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.318>Nay, come away.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt CORIOLANUS, COMINIUS, and others</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech117><b>A Patrician</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.319>This man has marr'd his fortune.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech118><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.320>His nature is too noble for the world:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.321>He would not flatter Neptune for his trident,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.322>Or Jove for's power to thunder. His heart's his mouth:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.323>What his breast forges, that his tongue must vent;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.324>And, being angry, does forget that ever</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.325>He heard the name of death.</p>
<p><i>A noise within</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.326>Here's goodly work!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech119><b>Second Patrician</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.327>I would they were abed!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech120><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.328>I would they were in Tiber! What the vengeance!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.329>Could he not speak 'em fair?</p>
<p><i>Re-enter BRUTUS and SICINIUS, with the rabble</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech121><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.330>Where is this viper</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.331>That would depopulate the city and</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.332>Be every man himself?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech122><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.333>You worthy tribunes,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech123><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.334>He shall be thrown down the Tarpeian rock</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.335>With rigorous hands: he hath resisted law,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.336>And therefore law shall scorn him further trial</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.337>Than the severity of the public power</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.338>Which he so sets at nought.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech124><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.339>He shall well know</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.340>The noble tribunes are the people's mouths,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.341>And we their hands.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech125><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.342>He shall, sure on't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech126><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.343>Sir, sir,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech127><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.344>Peace!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech128><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.345>Do not cry havoc, where you should but hunt</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.346>With modest warrant.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech129><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.347>Sir, how comes't that you</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.348>Have holp to make this rescue?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech130><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.349>Hear me speak:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.350>As I do know the consul's worthiness,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.351>So can I name his faults,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech131><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.352>Consul! what consul?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech132><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.353>The consul Coriolanus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech133><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.354>He consul!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech134><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.355>No, no, no, no, no.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech135><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.356>If, by the tribunes' leave, and yours, good people,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.357>I may be heard, I would crave a word or two;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.358>The which shall turn you to no further harm</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.359>Than so much loss of time.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech136><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.360>Speak briefly then;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.361>For we are peremptory to dispatch</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.362>This viperous traitor: to eject him hence</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.363>Were but one danger, and to keep him here</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.364>Our certain death: therefore it is decreed</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.365>He dies to-night.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech137><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.366>                  Now the good gods forbid</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.367>That our renowned Rome, whose gratitude</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.368>Towards her deserved children is enroll'd</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.369>In Jove's own book, like an unnatural dam</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.370>Should now eat up her own!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech138><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.371>He's a disease that must be cut away.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech139><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.372>O, he's a limb that has but a disease;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.373>Mortal, to cut it off; to cure it, easy.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.374>What has he done to Rome that's worthy death?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.375>Killing our enemies, the blood he hath lost--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.376>Which, I dare vouch, is more than that he hath,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.377>By many an ounce--he dropp'd it for his country;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.378>And what is left, to lose it by his country,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.379>Were to us all, that do't and suffer it,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.380>A brand to the end o' the world.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech140><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.381>This is clean kam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech141><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.382>Merely awry: when he did love his country,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.383>It honour'd him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech142><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.384>                  The service of the foot</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.385>Being once gangrened, is not then respected</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.386>For what before it was.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech143><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.387>We'll hear no more.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.388>Pursue him to his house, and pluck him thence:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.389>Lest his infection, being of catching nature,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.390>Spread further.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech144><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.391>                  One word more, one word.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.392>This tiger-footed rage, when it shall find</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.393>The harm of unscann'd swiftness, will too late</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.394>Tie leaden pounds to's heels. Proceed by process;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.395>Lest parties, as he is beloved, break out,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.396>And sack great Rome with Romans.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech145><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.397>If it were so,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech146><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.398>What do ye talk?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.399>Have we not had a taste of his obedience?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.400>Our aediles smote? ourselves resisted? Come.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech147><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.401>Consider this: he has been bred i' the wars</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.402>Since he could draw a sword, and is ill school'd</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.403>In bolted language; meal and bran together</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.404>He throws without distinction. Give me leave,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.405>I'll go to him, and undertake to bring him</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.406>Where he shall answer, by a lawful form,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.407>In peace, to his utmost peril.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech148><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.408>Noble tribunes,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.409>It is the humane way: the other course</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.410>Will prove too bloody, and the end of it</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.411>Unknown to the beginning.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech149><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.412>Noble Menenius,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.413>Be you then as the people's officer.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.414>Masters, lay down your weapons.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech150><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.415>Go not home.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech151><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.416>Meet on the market-place. We'll attend you there:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.417>Where, if you bring not Marcius, we'll proceed</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.418>In our first way.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech152><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.419>                  I'll bring him to you.</p>
<p><i>To the Senators</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.420>Let me desire your company: he must come,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.421>Or what is worst will follow.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech153><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.422>Pray you, let's to him.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. A room in CORIOLANUS'S house.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CORIOLANUS with Patricians</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.1>Let them puff all about mine ears, present me</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.2>Death on the wheel or at wild horses' heels,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.3>Or pile ten hills on the Tarpeian rock,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.4>That the precipitation might down stretch</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.5>Below the beam of sight, yet will I still</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.6>Be thus to them.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>A Patrician</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.7>You do the nobler.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.8>I muse my mother</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.9>Does not approve me further, who was wont</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.10>To call them woollen vassals, things created</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.11>To buy and sell with groats, to show bare heads</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.12>In congregations, to yawn, be still and wonder,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.13>When one but of my ordinance stood up</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.14>To speak of peace or war.</p>
<p><i>Enter VOLUMNIA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.15>I talk of you:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.16>Why did you wish me milder? would you have me</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.17>False to my nature? Rather say I play</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.18>The man I am.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.19>                  O, sir, sir, sir,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.20>I would have had you put your power well on,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.21>Before you had worn it out.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.22>Let go.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.23>You might have been enough the man you are,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.24>With striving less to be so; lesser had been</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.25>The thwartings of your dispositions, if</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.26>You had not show'd them how ye were disposed</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.27>Ere they lack'd power to cross you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.28>Let them hang.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>A Patrician</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.29>Ay, and burn too.</p>
<p><i>Enter MENENIUS and Senators</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.30>Come, come, you have been too rough, something</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.31>too rough;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.32>You must return and mend it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.33>There's no remedy;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.34>Unless, by not so doing, our good city</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.35>Cleave in the midst, and perish.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.36>Pray, be counsell'd:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.37>I have a heart as little apt as yours,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.38>But yet a brain that leads my use of anger</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.39>To better vantage.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.40>                  Well said, noble woman?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.41>Before he should thus stoop to the herd, but that</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.42>The violent fit o' the time craves it as physic</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.43>For the whole state, I would put mine armour on,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.44>Which I can scarcely bear.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.45>What must I do?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.46>Return to the tribunes.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.47>Well, what then? what then?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.48>Repent what you have spoke.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.49>For them! I cannot do it to the gods;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.50>Must I then do't to them?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.51>You are too absolute;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.52>Though therein you can never be too noble,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.53>But when extremities speak. I have heard you say,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.54>Honour and policy, like unsever'd friends,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.55>I' the war do grow together: grant that, and tell me,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.56>In peace what each of them by the other lose,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.57>That they combine not there.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.58>Tush, tush!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.59>A good demand.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.60>If it be honour in your wars to seem</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.61>The same you are not, which, for your best ends,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.62>You adopt your policy, how is it less or worse,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.63>That it shall hold companionship in peace</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.64>With honour, as in war, since that to both</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.65>It stands in like request?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.66>Why force you this?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.67>Because that now it lies you on to speak</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.68>To the people; not by your own instruction,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.69>Nor by the matter which your heart prompts you,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.70>But with such words that are but rooted in</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.71>Your tongue, though but bastards and syllables</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.72>Of no allowance to your bosom's truth.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.73>Now, this no more dishonours you at all</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.74>Than to take in a town with gentle words,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.75>Which else would put you to your fortune and</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.76>The hazard of much blood.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.77>I would dissemble with my nature where</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.78>My fortunes and my friends at stake required</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.79>I should do so in honour: I am in this,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.80>Your wife, your son, these senators, the nobles;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.81>And you will rather show our general louts</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.82>How you can frown than spend a fawn upon 'em,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.83>For the inheritance of their loves and safeguard</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.84>Of what that want might ruin.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.85>Noble lady!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.86>Come, go with us; speak fair: you may salve so,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.87>Not what is dangerous present, but the loss</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.88>Of what is past.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.89>                  I prithee now, my son,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.90>Go to them, with this bonnet in thy hand;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.91>And thus far having stretch'd it--here be with them--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.92>Thy knee bussing the stones--for in such business</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.93>Action is eloquence, and the eyes of the ignorant</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.94>More learned than the ears--waving thy head,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.95>Which often, thus, correcting thy stout heart,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.96>Now humble as the ripest mulberry</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.97>That will not hold the handling: or say to them,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.98>Thou art their soldier, and being bred in broils</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.99>Hast not the soft way which, thou dost confess,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.100>Were fit for thee to use as they to claim,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.101>In asking their good loves, but thou wilt frame</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.102>Thyself, forsooth, hereafter theirs, so far</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.103>As thou hast power and person.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.104>This but done,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.105>Even as she speaks, why, their hearts were yours;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.106>For they have pardons, being ask'd, as free</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.107>As words to little purpose.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.108>Prithee now,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.109>Go, and be ruled: although I know thou hadst rather</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.110>Follow thine enemy in a fiery gulf</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.111>Than flatter him in a bower. Here is Cominius.</p>
<p><i>Enter COMINIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.112>I have been i' the market-place; and, sir,'tis fit</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.113>You make strong party, or defend yourself</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.114>By calmness or by absence: all's in anger.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.115>Only fair speech.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.116>                  I think 'twill serve, if he</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.117>Can thereto frame his spirit.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.118>He must, and will</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.119>Prithee now, say you will, and go about it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.120>Must I go show them my unbarbed sconce?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.121>Must I with base tongue give my noble heart</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.122>A lie that it must bear? Well, I will do't:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.123>Yet, were there but this single plot to lose,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.124>This mould of Marcius, they to dust should grind it</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.125>And throw't against the wind. To the market-place!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.126>You have put me now to such a part which never</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.127>I shall discharge to the life.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.128>Come, come, we'll prompt you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.129>I prithee now, sweet son, as thou hast said</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.130>My praises made thee first a soldier, so,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.131>To have my praise for this, perform a part</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.132>Thou hast not done before.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.133>Well, I must do't:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.134>Away, my disposition, and possess me</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.135>Some harlot's spirit! my throat of war be turn'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.136>Which quired with my drum, into a pipe</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.137>Small as an eunuch, or the virgin voice</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.138>That babies lulls asleep! the smiles of knaves</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.139>Tent in my cheeks, and schoolboys' tears take up</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.140>The glasses of my sight! a beggar's tongue</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.141>Make motion through my lips, and my arm'd knees,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.142>Who bow'd but in my stirrup, bend like his</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.143>That hath received an alms! I will not do't,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.144>Lest I surcease to honour mine own truth</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.145>And by my body's action teach my mind</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.146>A most inherent baseness.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.147>At thy choice, then:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.148>To beg of thee, it is my more dishonour</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.149>Than thou of them. Come all to ruin; let</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.150>Thy mother rather feel thy pride than fear</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.151>Thy dangerous stoutness, for I mock at death</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.152>With as big heart as thou. Do as thou list</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.153>Thy valiantness was mine, thou suck'dst it from me,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.154>But owe thy pride thyself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.155>Pray, be content:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.156>Mother, I am going to the market-place;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.157>Chide me no more. I'll mountebank their loves,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.158>Cog their hearts from them, and come home beloved</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.159>Of all the trades in Rome. Look, I am going:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.160>Commend me to my wife. I'll return consul;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.161>Or never trust to what my tongue can do</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.162>I' the way of flattery further.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.163>Do your will.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.164>Away! the tribunes do attend you: arm yourself</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.165>To answer mildly; for they are prepared</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.166>With accusations, as I hear, more strong</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.167>Than are upon you yet.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.168>The word is 'mildly.' Pray you, let us go:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.169>Let them accuse me by invention, I</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.170>Will answer in mine honour.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.171>Ay, but mildly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.172>Well, mildly be it then. Mildly!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. The same. The Forum.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter SICINIUS and BRUTUS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.1>In this point charge him home, that he affects</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.2>Tyrannical power: if he evade us there,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.3>Enforce him with his envy to the people,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.4>And that the spoil got on the Antiates</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.5>Was ne'er distributed.</p>
<p><i>Enter an AEdile</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.6>What, will he come?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>AEdile</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.7>He's coming.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.8>How accompanied?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>AEdile</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.9>With old Menenius, and those senators</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.10>That always favour'd him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.11>Have you a catalogue</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.12>Of all the voices that we have procured</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.13>Set down by the poll?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>AEdile</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.14>I have; 'tis ready.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.15>Have you collected them by tribes?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>AEdile</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.16>I have.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.17>Assemble presently the people hither;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.18>And when they bear me say 'It shall be so</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.19>I' the right and strength o' the commons,' be it either</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.20>For death, for fine, or banishment, then let them</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.21>If I say fine, cry 'Fine;' if death, cry 'Death.'</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.22>Insisting on the old prerogative</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.23>And power i' the truth o' the cause.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>AEdile</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.24>I shall inform them.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.25>And when such time they have begun to cry,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.26>Let them not cease, but with a din confused</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.27>Enforce the present execution</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.28>Of what we chance to sentence.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>AEdile</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.29>Very well.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.30>Make them be strong and ready for this hint,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.31>When we shall hap to give 't them.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.32>Go about it.</p>
<p><i>Exit AEdile</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.33>Put him to choler straight: he hath been used</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.34>Ever to conquer, and to have his worth</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.35>Of contradiction: being once chafed, he cannot</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.36>Be rein'd again to temperance; then he speaks</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.37>What's in his heart; and that is there which looks</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.38>With us to break his neck.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.39>Well, here he comes.</p>
<p><i>Enter CORIOLANUS, MENENIUS, and COMINIUS, with Senators and Patricians</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.40>Calmly, I do beseech you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.41>Ay, as an ostler, that for the poorest piece</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.42>Will bear the knave by the volume. The honour'd gods</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.43>Keep Rome in safety, and the chairs of justice</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.44>Supplied with worthy men! plant love among 's!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.45>Throng our large temples with the shows of peace,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.46>And not our streets with war!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.47>Amen, amen.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.48>A noble wish.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter AEdile, with Citizens</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.49>Draw near, ye people.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>AEdile</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.50>List to your tribunes. Audience: peace, I say!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.51>First, hear me speak.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>Both Tribunes</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.52>Well, say. Peace, ho!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.53>Shall I be charged no further than this present?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.54>Must all determine here?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.55>I do demand,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.56>If you submit you to the people's voices,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.57>Allow their officers and are content</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.58>To suffer lawful censure for such faults</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.59>As shall be proved upon you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.60>I am content.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.61>Lo, citizens, he says he is content:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.62>The warlike service he has done, consider; think</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.63>Upon the wounds his body bears, which show</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.64>Like graves i' the holy churchyard.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.65>Scratches with briers,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.66>Scars to move laughter only.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.67>Consider further,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.68>That when he speaks not like a citizen,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.69>You find him like a soldier: do not take</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.70>His rougher accents for malicious sounds,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.71>But, as I say, such as become a soldier,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.72>Rather than envy you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.73>Well, well, no more.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.74>What is the matter</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.75>That being pass'd for consul with full voice,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.76>I am so dishonour'd that the very hour</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.77>You take it off again?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.78>Answer to us.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.79>Say, then: 'tis true, I ought so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.80>We charge you, that you have contrived to take</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.81>From Rome all season'd office and to wind</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.82>Yourself into a power tyrannical;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.83>For which you are a traitor to the people.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.84>How! traitor!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.85>                  Nay, temperately; your promise.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.86>The fires i' the lowest hell fold-in the people!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.87>Call me their traitor! Thou injurious tribune!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.88>Within thine eyes sat twenty thousand deaths,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.89>In thy hand clutch'd as many millions, in</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.90>Thy lying tongue both numbers, I would say</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.91>'Thou liest' unto thee with a voice as free</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.92>As I do pray the gods.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.93>Mark you this, people?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.94>To the rock, to the rock with him!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.95>Peace!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.96>We need not put new matter to his charge:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.97>What you have seen him do and heard him speak,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.98>Beating your officers, cursing yourselves,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.99>Opposing laws with strokes and here defying</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.100>Those whose great power must try him; even this,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.101>So criminal and in such capital kind,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.102>Deserves the extremest death.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.103>But since he hath</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.104>Served well for Rome,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.105>What do you prate of service?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.106>I talk of that, that know it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.107>You?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.108>Is this the promise that you made your mother?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.109>Know, I pray you,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.110>I know no further:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.111>Let them pronounce the steep Tarpeian death,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.112>Vagabond exile, raying, pent to linger</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.113>But with a grain a day, I would not buy</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.114>Their mercy at the price of one fair word;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.115>Nor cheque my courage for what they can give,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.116>To have't with saying 'Good morrow.'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.117>For that he has,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.118>As much as in him lies, from time to time</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.119>Envied against the people, seeking means</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.120>To pluck away their power, as now at last</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.121>Given hostile strokes, and that not in the presence</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.122>Of dreaded justice, but on the ministers</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.123>That do distribute it; in the name o' the people</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.124>And in the power of us the tribunes, we,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.125>Even from this instant, banish him our city,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.126>In peril of precipitation</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.127>From off the rock Tarpeian never more</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.128>To enter our Rome gates: i' the people's name,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.129>I say it shall be so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.130>It shall be so, it shall be so; let him away:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.131>He's banish'd, and it shall be so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.132>Hear me, my masters, and my common friends,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.133>He's sentenced; no more hearing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.134>Let me speak:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.135>I have been consul, and can show for Rome</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.136>Her enemies' marks upon me. I do love</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.137>My country's good with a respect more tender,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.138>More holy and profound, than mine own life,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.139>My dear wife's estimate, her womb's increase,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.140>And treasure of my loins; then if I would</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.141>Speak that,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.142>                  We know your drift: speak what?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.143>There's no more to be said, but he is banish'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.144>As enemy to the people and his country:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.145>It shall be so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.146>It shall be so, it shall be so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.147>You common cry of curs! whose breath I hate</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.148>As reek o' the rotten fens, whose loves I prize</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.149>As the dead carcasses of unburied men</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.150>That do corrupt my air, I banish you;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.151>And here remain with your uncertainty!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.152>Let every feeble rumour shake your hearts!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.153>Your enemies, with nodding of their plumes,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.154>Fan you into despair! Have the power still</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.155>To banish your defenders; till at length</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.156>Your ignorance, which finds not till it feels,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.157>Making not reservation of yourselves,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.158>Still your own foes, deliver you as most</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.159>Abated captives to some nation</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.160>That won you without blows! Despising,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.161>For you, the city, thus I turn my back:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.162>There is a world elsewhere.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt CORIOLANUS, COMINIUS, MENENIUS, Senators, and Patricians</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>AEdile</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.163>The people's enemy is gone, is gone!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.164>Our enemy is banish'd! he is gone! Hoo! hoo!</p>
<p><i>Shouting, and throwing up their caps</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.165>Go, see him out at gates, and follow him,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.166>As he hath followed you, with all despite;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.167>Give him deserved vexation. Let a guard</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.168>Attend us through the city.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.169>Come, come; let's see him out at gates; come.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.170>The gods preserve our noble tribunes! Come.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote><p>
<H3>ACT IV</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. Rome. Before a gate of the city.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CORIOLANUS, VOLUMNIA, VIRGILIA, MENENIUS, COMINIUS, with the young Nobility of Rome</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.1>Come, leave your tears: a brief farewell: the beast</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.2>With many heads butts me away. Nay, mother,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.3>Where is your ancient courage? you were used</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.4>To say extremity was the trier of spirits;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.5>That common chances common men could bear;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.6>That when the sea was calm all boats alike</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.7>Show'd mastership in floating; fortune's blows,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.8>When most struck home, being gentle wounded, craves</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.9>A noble cunning: you were used to load me</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.10>With precepts that would make invincible</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.11>The heart that conn'd them.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>VIRGILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.12>O heavens! O heavens!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.13>Nay! prithee, woman,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.14>Now the red pestilence strike all trades in Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.15>And occupations perish!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.16>What, what, what!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.17>I shall be loved when I am lack'd. Nay, mother.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.18>Resume that spirit, when you were wont to say,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.19>If you had been the wife of Hercules,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.20>Six of his labours you'ld have done, and saved</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.21>Your husband so much sweat. Cominius,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.22>Droop not; adieu. Farewell, my wife, my mother:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.23>I'll do well yet. Thou old and true Menenius,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.24>Thy tears are salter than a younger man's,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.25>And venomous to thine eyes. My sometime general,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.26>I have seen thee stem, and thou hast oft beheld</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.27>Heart-hardening spectacles; tell these sad women</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.28>'Tis fond to wail inevitable strokes,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.29>As 'tis to laugh at 'em. My mother, you wot well</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.30>My hazards still have been your solace: and</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.31>Believe't not lightly--though I go alone,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.32>Like to a lonely dragon, that his fen</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.33>Makes fear'd and talk'd of more than seen--your son</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.34>Will or exceed the common or be caught</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.35>With cautelous baits and practise.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.36>My first son.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.37>Whither wilt thou go? Take good Cominius</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.38>With thee awhile: determine on some course,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.39>More than a wild exposture to each chance</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.40>That starts i' the way before thee.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.41>O the gods!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.42>I'll follow thee a month, devise with thee</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.43>Where thou shalt rest, that thou mayst hear of us</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.44>And we of thee: so if the time thrust forth</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.45>A cause for thy repeal, we shall not send</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.46>O'er the vast world to seek a single man,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.47>And lose advantage, which doth ever cool</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.48>I' the absence of the needer.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.49>Fare ye well:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.50>Thou hast years upon thee; and thou art too full</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.51>Of the wars' surfeits, to go rove with one</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.52>That's yet unbruised: bring me but out at gate.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.53>Come, my sweet wife, my dearest mother, and</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.54>My friends of noble touch, when I am forth,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.55>Bid me farewell, and smile. I pray you, come.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.56>While I remain above the ground, you shall</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.57>Hear from me still, and never of me aught</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.58>But what is like me formerly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.59>That's worthily</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.60>As any ear can hear. Come, let's not weep.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.61>If I could shake off but one seven years</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.62>From these old arms and legs, by the good gods,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.1.63>I'ld with thee every foot.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.1.64>Give me thy hand: Come.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. The same. A  street near the gate.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter SICINIUS, BRUTUS, and an AEdile</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.1>Bid them all home; he's gone, and we'll no further.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.2>The nobility are vex'd, whom we see have sided</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.3>In his behalf.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.4>                  Now we have shown our power,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.5>Let us seem humbler after it is done</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.6>Than when it was a-doing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.7>Bid them home:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.8>Say their great enemy is gone, and they</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.9>Stand in their ancient strength.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.10>Dismiss them home.</p>
<p><i>Exit AEdile</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.11>Here comes his mother.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.12>Let's not meet her.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.13>Why?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.14>They say she's mad.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.15>They have ta'en note of us: keep on your way.</p>
<p><i>Enter VOLUMNIA, VIRGILIA, and MENENIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.16>O, ye're well met: the hoarded plague o' the gods</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.17>Requite your love!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.18>                  Peace, peace; be not so loud.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.19>If that I could for weeping, you should hear,--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.20>Nay, and you shall hear some.</p>
<p><i>To BRUTUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.21>Will you be gone?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>VIRGILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.22>[To SICINIUS]  You shall stay too: I would I had the power</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.23>To say so to my husband.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.24>Are  you mankind?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.25>Ay, fool; is that a shame? Note but this fool.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.26>Was not a man my father? Hadst thou foxship</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.27>To banish him that struck more blows for Rome</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.28>Than thou hast spoken words?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.29>O blessed heavens!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.30>More noble blows than ever thou wise words;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.31>And for Rome's good. I'll tell thee what; yet go:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.32>Nay, but thou shalt stay too: I would my son</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.33>Were in Arabia, and thy tribe before him,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.34>His good sword in his hand.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.35>What then?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>VIRGILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.36>What then!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.37>He'ld make an end of thy posterity.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.38>Bastards and all.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.39>Good man, the wounds that he does bear for Rome!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.40>Come, come, peace.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.41>I would he had continued to his country</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.42>As he began, and not unknit himself</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.43>The noble knot he made.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.44>I would he had.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.45>'I would he had'! 'Twas you incensed the rabble:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.46>Cats, that can judge as fitly of his worth</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.47>As I can of those mysteries which heaven</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.48>Will not have earth to know.</p>
</blockquote>
