<p class="line" name=speech24><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.49>Pray, let us go.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.50>Now, pray, sir, get you gone:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.51>You have done a brave deed. Ere you go, hear this:--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.52>As far as doth the Capitol exceed</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.53>The meanest house in Rome, so far my son--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.54>This lady's husband here, this, do you see--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.55>Whom you have banish'd, does exceed you all.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.56>Well, well, we'll leave you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.57>Why stay we to be baited</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.58>With one that wants her wits?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.59>Take my prayers with you.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt Tribunes</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.60>I would the gods had nothing else to do</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.61>But to confirm my curses! Could I meet 'em</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.62>But once a-day, it would unclog my heart</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.63>Of what lies heavy to't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.64>You have told them home;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.65>And, by my troth, you have cause. You'll sup with me?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.66>Anger's my meat; I sup upon myself,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.67>And so shall starve with feeding. Come, let's go:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.68>Leave this faint puling and lament as I do,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.2.69>In anger, Juno-like. Come, come, come.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.2.70>Fie, fie, fie!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. A highway between Rome and Antium.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter a Roman and a Volsce, meeting</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>Roman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.1>I know you well, sir, and you know</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.2>me: your name, I think, is Adrian.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Volsce</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.3>It is so, sir: truly, I have forgot you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>Roman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.4>I am a Roman; and my services are,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.5>as you are, against 'em: know you me yet?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Volsce</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.6>Nicanor? no.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>Roman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.7>The same, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Volsce</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.8>You had more beard when I last saw you; but your</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.9>favour is well approved by your tongue. What's the</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.10>news in Rome? I have a note from the Volscian state,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.11>to find you out there: you have well saved me a</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.12>day's journey.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>Roman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.13>There hath been in Rome strange insurrections; the</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.14>people against the senators, patricians, and nobles.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>Volsce</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.15>Hath been! is it ended, then? Our state thinks not</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.16>so: they are in a most warlike preparation, and</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.17>hope to come upon them in the heat of their division.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>Roman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.18>The main blaze of it is past, but a small thing</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.19>would make it flame again: for the nobles receive</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.20>so to heart the banishment of that worthy</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.21>Coriolanus, that they are in a ripe aptness to take</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.22>all power from the people and to pluck from them</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.23>their tribunes for ever. This lies glowing, I can</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.24>tell you, and is almost mature for the violent</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.25>breaking out.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Volsce</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.26>Coriolanus banished!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>Roman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.27>Banished, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>Volsce</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.28>You will be welcome with this intelligence, Nicanor.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>Roman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.29>The day serves well for them now. I have heard it</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.30>said, the fittest time to corrupt a man's wife is</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.31>when she's fallen out with her husband. Your noble</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.32>Tullus Aufidius will appear well in these wars, his</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.33>great opposer, Coriolanus, being now in no request</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.34>of his country.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>Volsce</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.35>He cannot choose. I am most fortunate, thus</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.36>accidentally to encounter you: you have ended my</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.37>business, and I will merrily accompany you home.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>Roman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.38>I shall, between this and supper, tell you most</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.39>strange things from Rome; all tending to the good of</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.40>their adversaries. Have you an army ready, say you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>Volsce</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.41>A most royal one; the centurions and their charges,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.42>distinctly billeted, already in the entertainment,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.43>and to be on foot at an hour's warning.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>Roman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.44>I am joyful to hear of their readiness, and am the</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.45>man, I think, that shall set them in present action.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.46>So, sir, heartily well met, and most glad of your company.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>Volsce</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.47>You take my part from me, sir; I have the most cause</p>
<p class="line" name=4.3.48>to be glad of yours.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>Roman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.3.49>Well, let us go together.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE IV. Antium. Before Aufidius's house.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CORIOLANUS in mean apparel, disguised and muffled</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.1>A goodly city is this Antium. City,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.2>'Tis I that made thy widows: many an heir</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.3>Of these fair edifices 'fore my wars</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.4>Have I heard groan and drop: then know me not,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.5>Lest that thy wives with spits and boys with stones</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.6>In puny battle slay me.</p>
<p><i>Enter a Citizen</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.7>Save you, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.8>And you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.9>       Direct me, if it be your will,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.10>Where great Aufidius lies: is he in Antium?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.11>He is, and feasts the nobles of the state</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.12>At his house this night.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.13>Which is his house, beseech you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.14>This, here before you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.4.15>Thank you, sir: farewell.</p>
<p><i>Exit Citizen</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.16>O world, thy slippery turns! Friends now fast sworn,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.17>Whose double bosoms seem to wear one heart,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.18>Whose house, whose bed, whose meal, and exercise,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.19>Are still together, who twin, as 'twere, in love</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.20>Unseparable, shall within this hour,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.21>On a dissension of a doit, break out</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.22>To bitterest enmity: so, fellest foes,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.23>Whose passions and whose plots have broke their sleep,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.24>To take the one the other, by some chance,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.25>Some trick not worth an egg, shall grow dear friends</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.26>And interjoin their issues. So with me:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.27>My birth-place hate I, and my love's upon</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.28>This enemy town. I'll enter: if he slay me,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.29>He does fair justice; if he give me way,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.4.30>I'll do his country service.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE V. The same. A hall in Aufidius's house.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Music within. Enter a Servingman</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.1>Wine, wine, wine! What service</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.2>is here! I think our fellows are asleep.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<p><i>Enter a second Servingman</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.3>Where's Cotus? my master calls</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.4>for him. Cotus!</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
<p><i>Enter CORIOLANUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.5>A goodly house: the feast smells well; but I</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.6>Appear not like a guest.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter the first Servingman</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.7>What would you have, friend? whence are you?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.8>Here's no place for you: pray, go to the door.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.9>I have deserved no better entertainment,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.10>In being Coriolanus.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter second Servingman</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.11>Whence are you, sir? Has the porter his eyes in his</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.12>head; that he gives entrance to such companions?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.13>Pray, get you out.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.14>Away!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.15>Away! get you away.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.16>Now thou'rt troublesome.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.17>Are you so brave? I'll have you talked with anon.</p>
<p><i>Enter a third Servingman. The first meets him</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.18>What fellow's this?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.19>A strange one as ever I looked on: I cannot get him</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.20>out of the house: prithee, call my master to him.</p>
<p><i>Retires</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.21>What have you to do here, fellow? Pray you, avoid</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.22>the house.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.23>Let me but stand; I will not hurt your hearth.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.24>What are you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.25>A gentleman.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.26>A marvellous poor one.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.27>True, so I am.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.28>Pray you, poor gentleman, take up some other</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.29>station; here's no place for you; pray you, avoid: come.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.30>Follow your function, go, and batten on cold bits.</p>
<p><i>Pushes him away</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.31>What, you will not? Prithee, tell my master what a</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.32>strange guest he has here.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.33>And I shall.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.34>Where dwellest thou?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.35>Under the canopy.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.36>Under the canopy!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.37>Ay.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.38>Where's that?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.39>I' the city of kites and crows.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.40>I' the city of kites and crows! What an ass it is!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.41>Then thou dwellest with daws too?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.42>No, I serve not thy master.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.43>How, sir! do you meddle with my master?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.44>Ay; 'tis an honester service than to meddle with thy</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.45>mistress. Thou pratest, and pratest; serve with thy</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.46>trencher, hence!</p>
<p><i>Beats him away. Exit third Servingman</i></p>
<p><i>Enter AUFIDIUS with the second Servingman</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.47>Where is this fellow?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.48>Here, sir: I'ld have beaten him like a dog, but for</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.49>disturbing the lords within.</p>
<p><i>Retires</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.50>Whence comest thou? what wouldst thou? thy name?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.51>Why speak'st not? speak, man: what's thy name?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.52>If, Tullus,</p>
<p><i>Unmuffling</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.53>Not yet thou knowest me, and, seeing me, dost not</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.54>Think me for the man I am, necessity</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.55>Commands me name myself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.56>What is thy name?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.57>A name unmusical to the Volscians' ears,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.58>And harsh in sound to thine.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.59>Say, what's thy name?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.60>Thou hast a grim appearance, and thy face</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.61>Bears a command in't; though thy tackle's torn.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.62>Thou show'st a noble vessel: what's thy name?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.63>Prepare thy brow to frown: know'st</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.64>thou me yet?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.65>I know thee not: thy name?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.66>My name is Caius Marcius, who hath done</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.67>To thee particularly and to all the Volsces</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.68>Great hurt and mischief; thereto witness may</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.69>My surname, Coriolanus: the painful service,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.70>The extreme dangers and the drops of blood</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.71>Shed for my thankless country are requited</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.72>But with that surname; a good memory,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.73>And witness of the malice and displeasure</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.74>Which thou shouldst bear me: only that name remains;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.75>The cruelty and envy of the people,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.76>Permitted by our dastard nobles, who</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.77>Have all forsook me, hath devour'd the rest;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.78>And suffer'd me by the voice of slaves to be</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.79>Whoop'd out of Rome. Now this extremity</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.80>Hath brought me to thy hearth; not out of hope--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.81>Mistake me not--to save my life, for if</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.82>I had fear'd death, of all the men i' the world</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.83>I would have 'voided thee, but in mere spite,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.84>To be full quit of those my banishers,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.85>Stand I before thee here. Then if thou hast</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.86>A heart of wreak in thee, that wilt revenge</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.87>Thine own particular wrongs and stop those maims</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.88>Of shame seen through thy country, speed</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.89>thee straight,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.90>And make my misery serve thy turn: so use it</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.91>That my revengeful services may prove</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.92>As benefits to thee, for I will fight</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.93>Against my canker'd country with the spleen</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.94>Of all the under fiends. But if so be</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.95>Thou darest not this and that to prove more fortunes</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.96>Thou'rt tired, then, in a word, I also am</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.97>Longer to live most weary, and present</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.98>My throat to thee and to thy ancient malice;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.99>Which not to cut would show thee but a fool,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.100>Since I have ever follow'd thee with hate,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.101>Drawn tuns of blood out of thy country's breast,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.102>And cannot live but to thy shame, unless</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.103>It be to do thee service.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.104>O Marcius, Marcius!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.105>Each word thou hast spoke hath weeded from my heart</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.106>A root of ancient envy. If Jupiter</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.107>Should from yond cloud speak divine things,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.108>And say 'Tis true,' I'ld not believe them more</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.109>Than thee, all noble Marcius. Let me twine</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.110>Mine arms about that body, where against</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.111>My grained ash an hundred times hath broke</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.112>And scarr'd the moon with splinters: here I clip</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.113>The anvil of my sword, and do contest</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.114>As hotly and as nobly with thy love</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.115>As ever in ambitious strength I did</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.116>Contend against thy valour. Know thou first,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.117>I loved the maid I married; never man</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.118>Sigh'd truer breath; but that I see thee here,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.119>Thou noble thing! more dances my rapt heart</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.120>Than when I first my wedded mistress saw</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.121>Bestride my threshold. Why, thou Mars! I tell thee,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.122>We have a power on foot; and I had purpose</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.123>Once more to hew thy target from thy brawn,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.124>Or lose mine arm fort: thou hast beat me out</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.125>Twelve several times, and I have nightly since</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.126>Dreamt of encounters 'twixt thyself and me;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.127>We have been down together in my sleep,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.128>Unbuckling helms, fisting each other's throat,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.129>And waked half dead with nothing. Worthy Marcius,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.130>Had we no quarrel else to Rome, but that</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.131>Thou art thence banish'd, we would muster all</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.132>From twelve to seventy, and pouring war</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.133>Into the bowels of ungrateful Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.134>Like a bold flood o'er-bear. O, come, go in,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.135>And take our friendly senators by the hands;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.136>Who now are here, taking their leaves of me,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.137>Who am prepared against your territories,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.138>Though not for Rome itself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.139>You bless me, gods!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.140>Therefore, most absolute sir, if thou wilt have</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.141>The leading of thine own revenges, take</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.142>The one half of my commission; and set down--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.143>As best thou art experienced, since thou know'st</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.144>Thy country's strength and weakness,--thine own ways;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.145>Whether to knock against the gates of Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.146>Or rudely visit them in parts remote,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.147>To fright them, ere destroy. But come in:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.148>Let me commend thee first to those that shall</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.149>Say yea to thy desires. A thousand welcomes!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.150>And more a friend than e'er an enemy;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.151>Yet, Marcius, that was much. Your hand: most welcome!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt CORIOLANUS and AUFIDIUS. The two Servingmen come forward</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.152>Here's a strange alteration!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.153>By my hand, I had thought to have strucken him with</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.154>a cudgel; and yet my mind gave me his clothes made a</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.155>false report of him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.156>What an arm he has! he turned me about with his</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.157>finger and his thumb, as one would set up a top.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.158>Nay, I knew by his face that there was something in</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.159>him: he had, sir, a kind of face, methought,--I</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.160>cannot tell how to term it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.161>He had so; looking as it were--would I were hanged,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.162>but I thought there was more in him than I could think.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.163>So did I, I'll be sworn: he is simply the rarest</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.164>man i' the world.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.165>I think he is: but a greater soldier than he you wot on.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.166>Who, my master?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.167>Nay, it's no matter for that.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.168>Worth six on him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.169>Nay, not so neither: but I take him to be the</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.170>greater soldier.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.171>Faith, look you, one cannot tell how to say that:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.172>for the defence of a town, our general is excellent.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.173>Ay, and for an assault too.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter third Servingman</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.174>O slaves, I can tell you news,-- news, you rascals!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>First Servingman</b></p>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.175>What, what, what? let's partake.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.176>I would not be a Roman, of all nations; I had as</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.177>lieve be a condemned man.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>First Servingman</b></p>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.178>Wherefore? wherefore?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.179>Why, here's he that was wont to thwack our general,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.180>Caius Marcius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.181>Why do you say 'thwack our general '?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.182>I do not say 'thwack our general;' but he was always</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.183>good enough for him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.184>Come, we are fellows and friends: he was ever too</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.185>hard for him; I have heard him say so himself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.186>He was too hard for him directly, to say the troth</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.187>on't: before Corioli he scotched him and notched</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.188>him like a carbon ado.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.189>An he had been cannibally given, he might have</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.190>broiled and eaten him too.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.191>But, more of thy news?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.192>Why, he is so made on here within, as if he were son</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.193>and heir to Mars; set at upper end o' the table; no</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.194>question asked him by any of the senators, but they</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.195>stand bald before him: our general himself makes a</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.196>mistress of him: sanctifies himself with's hand and</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.197>turns up the white o' the eye to his discourse. But</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.198>the bottom of the news is that our general is cut i'</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.199>the middle and but one half of what he was</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.200>yesterday; for the other has half, by the entreaty</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.201>and grant of the whole table. He'll go, he says,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.202>and sowl the porter of Rome gates by the ears: he</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.203>will mow all down before him, and leave his passage polled.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.204>And he's as like to do't as any man I can imagine.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.205>Do't! he will do't; for, look you, sir, he has as</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.206>many friends as enemies; which friends, sir, as it</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.207>were, durst not, look you, sir, show themselves, as</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.208>we term it, his friends whilst he's in directitude.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech75><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.209>Directitude! what's that?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech76><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.210>But when they shall see, sir, his crest up again,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.211>and the man in blood, they will out of their</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.212>burrows, like conies after rain, and revel all with</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.213>him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech77><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.214>But when goes this forward?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech78><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.215>To-morrow; to-day; presently; you shall have the</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.216>drum struck up this afternoon: 'tis, as it were, a</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.217>parcel of their feast, and to be executed ere they</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.218>wipe their lips.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech79><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.219>Why, then we shall have a stirring world again.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.220>This peace is nothing, but to rust iron, increase</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.221>tailors, and breed ballad-makers.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech80><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.222>Let me have war, say I; it exceeds peace as far as</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.223>day does night; it's spritely, waking, audible, and</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.224>full of vent. Peace is a very apoplexy, lethargy;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.225>mulled, deaf, sleepy, insensible; a getter of more</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.226>bastard children than war's a destroyer of men.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech81><b>Second Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.227>'Tis so: and as war, in some sort, may be said to</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.228>be a ravisher, so it cannot be denied but peace is a</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.229>great maker of cuckolds.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech82><b>First Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.230>Ay, and it makes men hate one another.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech83><b>Third Servingman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.231>Reason; because they then less need one another.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.232>The wars for my money. I hope to see Romans as cheap</p>
<p class="line" name=4.5.233>as Volscians. They are rising, they are rising.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech84><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.5.234>In, in, in, in!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE VI. Rome. A public place.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter SICINIUS and BRUTUS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.1>We hear not of him, neither need we fear him;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.2>His remedies are tame i' the present peace</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.3>And quietness of the people, which before</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.4>Were in wild hurry. Here do we make his friends</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.5>Blush that the world goes well, who rather had,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.6>Though they themselves did suffer by't, behold</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.7>Dissentious numbers pestering streets than see</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.8>Our tradesmen with in their shops and going</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.9>About their functions friendly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.10>We stood to't in good time.</p>
<p><i>Enter MENENIUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.11>Is this Menenius?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.12>'Tis he,'tis he: O, he is grown most kind of late.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Both Tribunes</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.13>Hail sir!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.14>        Hail to you both!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.15>Your Coriolanus</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.16>Is not much miss'd, but with his friends:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.17>The commonwealth doth stand, and so would do,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.18>Were he more angry at it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.19>All's well; and might have been much better, if</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.20>He could have temporized.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.21>Where is he, hear you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.22>Nay, I hear nothing: his mother and his wife</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.23>Hear nothing from him.</p>
<p><i>Enter three or four Citizens</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.24>The gods preserve you both!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.25>God-den, our neighbours.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.26>God-den to you all, god-den to you all.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.27>Ourselves, our wives, and children, on our knees,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.28>Are bound to pray for you both.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.29>Live, and thrive!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.30>Farewell, kind neighbours: we wish'd Coriolanus</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.31>Had loved you as we did.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.32>Now the gods keep you!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>Both Tribunes</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.33>Farewell, farewell.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt Citizens</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.34>This is a happier and more comely time</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.35>Than when these fellows ran about the streets,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.36>Crying confusion.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.37>                  Caius Marcius was</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.38>A worthy officer i' the war; but insolent,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.39>O'ercome with pride, ambitious past all thinking,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.40>Self-loving,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.41>                  And affecting one sole throne,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.42>Without assistance.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.43>I think not so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.44>We should by this, to all our lamentation,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.45>If he had gone forth consul, found it so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.46>The gods have well prevented it, and Rome</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.47>Sits safe and still without him.</p>
<p><i>Enter an AEdile</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>AEdile</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.48>Worthy tribunes,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.49>There is a slave, whom we have put in prison,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.50>Reports, the Volsces with two several powers</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.51>Are enter'd in the Roman territories,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.52>And with the deepest malice of the war</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.53>Destroy what lies before 'em.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.54>'Tis Aufidius,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.55>Who, hearing of our Marcius' banishment,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.56>Thrusts forth his horns again into the world;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.57>Which were inshell'd when Marcius stood for Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.58>And durst not once peep out.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.59>Come, what talk you</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.60>Of Marcius?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.61>Go see this rumourer whipp'd. It cannot be</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.62>The Volsces dare break with us.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.63>Cannot be!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.64>We have record that very well it can,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.65>And three examples of the like have been</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.66>Within my age. But reason with the fellow,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.67>Before you punish him, where he heard this,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.68>Lest you shall chance to whip your information</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.69>And beat the messenger who bids beware</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.70>Of what is to be dreaded.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.71>Tell not me:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.72>I know this cannot be.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.73>Not possible.</p>
<p><i>Enter a Messenger</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.74>The nobles in great earnestness are going</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.75>All to the senate-house: some news is come</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.76>That turns their countenances.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.77>'Tis this slave;--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.78>Go whip him, 'fore the people's eyes:--his raising;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.79>Nothing but his report.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.80>Yes, worthy sir,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.81>The slave's report is seconded; and more,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.82>More fearful, is deliver'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.83>What more fearful?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.84>It is spoke freely out of many mouths--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.85>How probable I do not know--that Marcius,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.86>Join'd with Aufidius, leads a power 'gainst Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.87>And vows revenge as spacious as between</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.88>The young'st and oldest thing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.89>This is most likely!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.90>Raised only, that the weaker sort may wish</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.91>Good Marcius home again.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.92>The very trick on't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.93>This is unlikely:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.94>He and Aufidius can no more atone</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.95>Than violentest contrariety.</p>
<p><i>Enter a second Messenger</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>Second Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.96>You are sent for to the senate:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.97>A fearful army, led by Caius Marcius</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.98>Associated with Aufidius, rages</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.99>Upon our territories; and have already</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.100>O'erborne their way, consumed with fire, and took</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.101>What lay before them.</p>
<p><i>Enter COMINIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.102>O, you have made good work!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.103>What news? what news?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.104>You have holp to ravish your own daughters and</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.105>To melt the city leads upon your pates,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.106>To see your wives dishonour'd to your noses,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.107>What's the news? what's the news?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.108>Your temples burned in their cement, and</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.109>Your franchises, whereon you stood, confined</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.110>Into an auger's bore.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.111>Pray now, your news?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.112>You have made fair work, I fear me.--Pray, your news?--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.113>If Marcius should be join'd with Volscians,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.114>If!</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.115>He is their god: he leads them like a thing</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.116>Made by some other deity than nature,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.117>That shapes man better; and they follow him,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.118>Against us brats, with no less confidence</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.119>Than boys pursuing summer butterflies,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.120>Or butchers killing flies.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.121>You have made good work,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.122>You and your apron-men; you that stood so up much</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.123>on the voice of occupation and</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.124>The breath of garlic-eaters!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.125>He will shake</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.126>Your Rome about your ears.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.127>As Hercules</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.128>Did shake down mellow fruit.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.129>You have made fair work!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.130>But is this true, sir?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.131>Ay; and you'll look pale</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.132>Before you find it other. All the regions</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.133>Do smilingly revolt; and who resist</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.134>Are mock'd for valiant ignorance,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.135>And perish constant fools. Who is't can blame him?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.136>Your enemies and his find something in him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.137>We are all undone, unless</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.138>The noble man have mercy.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.139>Who shall ask it?</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.140>The tribunes cannot do't for shame; the people</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.141>Deserve such pity of him as the wolf</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.142>Does of the shepherds: for his best friends, if they</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.143>Should say 'Be good to Rome,' they charged him even</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.144>As those should do that had deserved his hate,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.145>And therein show'd like enemies.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.146>'Tis true:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.147>If he were putting to my house the brand</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.148>That should consume it, I have not the face</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.149>To say 'Beseech you, cease.' You have made fair hands,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.150>You and your crafts! you have crafted fair!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.151>You have brought</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.152>A trembling upon Rome, such as was never</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.153>So incapable of help.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>Both Tribunes</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.154>Say not we brought it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.155>How! Was it we? we loved him but, like beasts</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.156>And cowardly nobles, gave way unto your clusters,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.157>Who did hoot him out o' the city.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.158>But I fear</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.159>They'll roar him in again. Tullus Aufidius,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.160>The second name of men, obeys his points</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.161>As if he were his officer: desperation</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.162>Is all the policy, strength and defence,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.163>That Rome can make against them.</p>
<p><i>Enter a troop of Citizens</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.164>Here come the clusters.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.165>And is Aufidius with him? You are they</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.166>That made the air unwholesome, when you cast</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.167>Your stinking greasy caps in hooting at</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.168>Coriolanus' exile. Now he's coming;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.169>And not a hair upon a soldier's head</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.170>Which will not prove a whip: as many coxcombs</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.171>As you threw caps up will he tumble down,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.172>And pay you for your voices. 'Tis no matter;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.173>if he could burn us all into one coal,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.174>We have deserved it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>Citizens</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.175>Faith, we hear fearful news.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.176>For mine own part,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.177>When I said, banish him, I said 'twas pity.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.178>And so did I.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>Third Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.179>And so did I; and, to say the truth, so did very</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.180>many of us: that we did, we did for the best; and</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.181>though we willingly consented to his banishment, yet</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.182>it was against our will.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.183>Ye re goodly things, you voices!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.184>You have made</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.185>Good work, you and your cry! Shall's to the Capitol?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.186>O, ay, what else?</p>
<p><i>Exeunt COMINIUS and MENENIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.187>Go, masters, get you home; be not dismay'd:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.188>These are a side that would be glad to have</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.189>This true which they so seem to fear. Go home,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.190>And show no sign of fear.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>First Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.191>The gods be good to us! Come, masters, let's home.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.192>I ever said we were i' the wrong when we banished</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.193>him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>Second Citizen</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.194>So did we all. But, come, let's home.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt Citizens</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.195>I do not like this news.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.196>Nor I.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.197>Let's to the Capitol. Would half my wealth</p>
<p class="line" name=4.6.198>Would buy this for a lie!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.6.199>Pray, let us go.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE VII. A camp, at a small distance from Rome.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter AUFIDIUS and his Lieutenant</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.1>Do they still fly to the Roman?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Lieutenant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.2>I do not know what witchcraft's in him, but</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.3>Your soldiers use him as the grace 'fore meat,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.4>Their talk at table, and their thanks at end;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.5>And you are darken'd in this action, sir,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.6>Even by your own.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.7>                  I cannot help it now,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.8>Unless, by using means, I lame the foot</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.9>Of our design. He bears himself more proudlier,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.10>Even to my person, than I thought he would</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.11>When first I did embrace him: yet his nature</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.12>In that's no changeling; and I must excuse</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.13>What cannot be amended.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Lieutenant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.14>Yet I wish, sir,--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.15>I mean for your particular,--you had not</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.16>Join'd in commission with him; but either</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.17>Had borne the action of yourself, or else</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.18>To him had left it solely.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.19>I understand thee well; and be thou sure,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.20>when he shall come to his account, he knows not</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.21>What I can urge against him. Although it seems,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.22>And so he thinks, and is no less apparent</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.23>To the vulgar eye, that he bears all things fairly.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.24>And shows good husbandry for the Volscian state,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.25>Fights dragon-like, and does achieve as soon</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.26>As draw his sword; yet he hath left undone</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.27>That which shall break his neck or hazard mine,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.28>Whene'er we come to our account.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Lieutenant</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.29>Sir, I beseech you, think you he'll carry Rome?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=4.7.30>All places yield to him ere he sits down;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.31>And the nobility of Rome are his:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.32>The senators and patricians love him too:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.33>The tribunes are no soldiers; and their people</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.34>Will be as rash in the repeal, as hasty</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.35>To expel him thence. I think he'll be to Rome</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.36>As is the osprey to the fish, who takes it</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.37>By sovereignty of nature. First he was</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.38>A noble servant to them; but he could not</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.39>Carry his honours even: whether 'twas pride,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.40>Which out of daily fortune ever taints</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.41>The happy man; whether defect of judgment,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.42>To fail in the disposing of those chances</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.43>Which he was lord of; or whether nature,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.44>Not to be other than one thing, not moving</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.45>From the casque to the cushion, but commanding peace</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.46>Even with the same austerity and garb</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.47>As he controll'd the war; but one of these--</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.48>As he hath spices of them all, not all,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.49>For I dare so far free him--made him fear'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.50>So hated, and so banish'd: but he has a merit,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.51>To choke it in the utterance. So our virtues</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.52>Lie in the interpretation of the time:</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.53>And power, unto itself most commendable,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.54>Hath not a tomb so evident as a chair</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.55>To extol what it hath done.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.56>One fire drives out one fire; one nail, one nail;</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.57>Rights by rights falter, strengths by strengths do fail.</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.58>Come, let's away. When, Caius, Rome is thine,</p>
<p class="line" name=4.7.59>Thou art poor'st of all; then shortly art thou mine.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote><p>
<H3>ACT V</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. Rome. A public place.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter MENENIUS, COMINIUS, SICINIUS, BRUTUS, and others</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.1>No, I'll not go: you hear what he hath said</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.2>Which was sometime his general; who loved him</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.3>In a most dear particular. He call'd me father:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.4>But what o' that? Go, you that banish'd him;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.5>A mile before his tent fall down, and knee</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.6>The way into his mercy: nay, if he coy'd</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.7>To hear Cominius speak, I'll keep at home.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.8>He would not seem to know me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.9>Do you hear?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.10>Yet one time he did call me by my name:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.11>I urged our old acquaintance, and the drops</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.12>That we have bled together. Coriolanus</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.13>He would not answer to: forbad all names;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.14>He was a kind of nothing, titleless,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.15>Till he had forged himself a name o' the fire</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.16>Of burning Rome.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.17>Why, so: you have made good work!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.18>A pair of tribunes that have rack'd for Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.19>To make coals cheap,--a noble memory!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.20>I minded him how royal 'twas to pardon</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.21>When it was less expected: he replied,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.22>It was a bare petition of a state</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.23>To one whom they had punish'd.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.24>Very well:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.25>Could he say less?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.26>I offer'd to awaken his regard</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.27>For's private friends: his answer to me was,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.28>He could not stay to pick them in a pile</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.29>Of noisome musty chaff: he said 'twas folly,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.30>For one poor grain or two, to leave unburnt,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.31>And still to nose the offence.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.32>For one poor grain or two!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.33>I am one of those; his mother, wife, his child,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.34>And this brave fellow too, we are the grains:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.35>You are the musty chaff; and you are smelt</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.36>Above the moon: we must be burnt for you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.37>Nay, pray, be patient: if you refuse your aid</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.38>In this so never-needed help, yet do not</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.39>Upbraid's with our distress. But, sure, if you</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.40>Would be your country's pleader, your good tongue,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.41>More than the instant army we can make,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.42>Might stop our countryman.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.43>No, I'll not meddle.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.44>Pray you, go to him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.45>What should I do?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.46>Only make trial what your love can do</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.47>For Rome, towards Marcius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.48>Well, and say that Marcius</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.49>Return me, as Cominius is return'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.50>Unheard; what then?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.51>But as a discontented friend, grief-shot</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.52>With his unkindness? say't be so?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.53>Yet your good will</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.54>must have that thanks from Rome, after the measure</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.55>As you intended well.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.56>I'll undertake 't:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.57>I think he'll hear me. Yet, to bite his lip</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.58>And hum at good Cominius, much unhearts me.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.59>He was not taken well; he had not dined:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.60>The veins unfill'd, our blood is cold, and then</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.61>We pout upon the morning, are unapt</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.62>To give or to forgive; but when we have stuff'd</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.63>These and these conveyances of our blood</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.64>With wine and feeding, we have suppler souls</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.65>Than in our priest-like fasts: therefore I'll watch him</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.66>Till he be dieted to my request,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.67>And then I'll set upon him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>BRUTUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.68>You know the very road into his kindness,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.69>And cannot lose your way.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.70>Good faith, I'll prove him,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.71>Speed how it will. I shall ere long have knowledge</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.72>Of my success.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.73>                  He'll never hear him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.74>Not?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>COMINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.1.75>I tell you, he does sit in gold, his eye</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.76>Red as 'twould burn Rome; and his injury</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.77>The gaoler to his pity. I kneel'd before him;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.78>'Twas very faintly he said 'Rise;' dismiss'd me</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.79>Thus, with his speechless hand: what he would do,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.80>He sent in writing after me; what he would not,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.81>Bound with an oath to yield to his conditions:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.82>So that all hope is vain.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.83>Unless his noble mother, and his wife;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.84>Who, as I hear, mean to solicit him</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.85>For mercy to his country. Therefore, let's hence,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.1.86>And with our fair entreaties haste them on.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. Entrance of the Volscian camp before Rome.</h3>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.1>Two Sentinels on guard.</p>
<p><i>Enter to them, MENENIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.2>Stay: whence are you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Second Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.3>Stand, and go back.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.4>You guard like men; 'tis well: but, by your leave,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.5>I am an officer of state, and come</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.6>To speak with Coriolanus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.7>From whence?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.8>From Rome.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.9>You may not pass, you must return: our general</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.10>Will no more hear from thence.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>Second Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.11>You'll see your Rome embraced with fire before</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.12>You'll speak with Coriolanus.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.13>Good my friends,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.14>If you have heard your general talk of Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.15>And of his friends there, it is lots to blanks,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.16>My name hath touch'd your ears it is Menenius.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.17>Be it so; go back: the virtue of your name</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.18>Is not here passable.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.19>I tell thee, fellow,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.20>The general is my lover: I have been</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.21>The book of his good acts, whence men have read</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.22>His name unparallel'd, haply amplified;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.23>For I have ever verified my friends,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.24>Of whom he's chief, with all the size that verity</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.25>Would without lapsing suffer: nay, sometimes,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.26>Like to a bowl upon a subtle ground,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.27>I have tumbled past the throw; and in his praise</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.28>Have almost stamp'd the leasing: therefore, fellow,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.29>I must have leave to pass.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.30>Faith, sir, if you had told as many lies in his</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.31>behalf as you have uttered words in your own, you</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.32>should not pass here; no, though it were as virtuous</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.33>to lie as to live chastely. Therefore, go back.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.34>Prithee, fellow, remember my name is Menenius,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.35>always factionary on the party of your general.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>Second Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.36>Howsoever you have been his liar, as you say you</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.37>have, I am one that, telling true under him, must</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.38>say, you cannot pass. Therefore, go back.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.39>Has he dined, canst thou tell? for I would not</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.40>speak with him till after dinner.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.41>You are a Roman, are you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.42>I am, as thy general is.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.43>Then you should hate Rome, as he does. Can you,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.44>when you have pushed out your gates the very</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.45>defender of them, and, in a violent popular</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.46>ignorance, given your enemy your shield, think to</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.47>front his revenges with the easy groans of old</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.48>women, the virginal palms of your daughters, or with</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.49>the palsied intercession of such a decayed dotant as</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.50>you seem to be? Can you think to blow out the</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.51>intended fire your city is ready to flame in, with</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.52>such weak breath as this? No, you are deceived;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.53>therefore, back to Rome, and prepare for your</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.54>execution: you are condemned, our general has sworn</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.55>you out of reprieve and pardon.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.56>Sirrah, if thy captain knew I were here, he would</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.57>use me with estimation.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>Second Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.58>Come, my captain knows you not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.59>I mean, thy general.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.60>My general cares not for you. Back, I say, go; lest</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.61>I let forth your half-pint of blood; back,--that's</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.62>the utmost of your having: back.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.63>Nay, but, fellow, fellow,--</p>
<p><i>Enter CORIOLANUS and AUFIDIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.64>What's the matter?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.65>Now, you companion, I'll say an errand for you:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.66>You shall know now that I am in estimation; you shall</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.67>perceive that a Jack guardant cannot office me from</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.68>my son Coriolanus: guess, but by my entertainment</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.69>with him, if thou standest not i' the state of</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.70>hanging, or of some death more long in</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.71>spectatorship, and crueller in suffering; behold now</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.72>presently, and swoon for what's to come upon thee.</p>
<p><i>To CORIOLANUS</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.73>The glorious gods sit in hourly synod about thy</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.74>particular prosperity, and love thee no worse than</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.75>thy old father Menenius does! O my son, my son!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.76>thou art preparing fire for us; look thee, here's</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.77>water to quench it. I was hardly moved to come to</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.78>thee; but being assured none but myself could move</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.79>thee, I have been blown out of your gates with</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.80>sighs; and conjure thee to pardon Rome, and thy</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.81>petitionary countrymen. The good gods assuage thy</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.82>wrath, and turn the dregs of it upon this varlet</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.83>here,--this, who, like a block, hath denied my</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.84>access to thee.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.85>Away!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.86>How! away!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.87>Wife, mother, child, I know not. My affairs</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.88>Are servanted to others: though I owe</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.89>My revenge properly, my remission lies</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.90>In Volscian breasts. That we have been familiar,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.91>Ingrate forgetfulness shall poison, rather</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.92>Than pity note how much. Therefore, be gone.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.93>Mine ears against your suits are stronger than</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.94>Your gates against my force. Yet, for I loved thee,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.95>Take this along; I writ it for thy sake</p>
<p><i>Gives a letter</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.96>And would have rent it. Another word, Menenius,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.97>I will not hear thee speak. This man, Aufidius,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.98>Was my beloved in Rome: yet thou behold'st!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.99>You keep a constant temper.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt CORIOLANUS and AUFIDIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.100>Now, sir, is your name Menenius?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>Second Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.101>'Tis a spell, you see, of much  power: you know the</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.102>way home again.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.103>Do you hear how we are shent for keeping your</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.104>greatness back?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>Second Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.105>What cause, do you think, I have to swoon?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.106>I neither care for the world nor your general: for</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.107>such things as you, I can scarce think there's any,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.108>ye're so slight. He that hath a will to die by</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.109>himself fears it not from another: let your general</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.110>do his worst. For you, be that you are, long; and</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.111>your misery increase with your age! I say to you,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.112>as I was said to, Away!</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.113>A noble fellow, I warrant him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>Second Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.2.114>The worthy fellow is our general: he's the rock, the</p>
<p class="line" name=5.2.115>oak not to be wind-shaken.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. The tent of Coriolanus.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CORIOLANUS, AUFIDIUS, and others</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.1>We will before the walls of Rome tomorrow</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.2>Set down our host. My partner in this action,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.3>You must report to the Volscian lords, how plainly</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.4>I have borne this business.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.5>Only their ends</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.6>You have respected; stopp'd your ears against</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.7>The general suit of Rome; never admitted</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.8>A private whisper, no, not with such friends</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.9>That thought them sure of you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.10>This last old man,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.11>Whom with a crack'd heart I have sent to Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.12>Loved me above the measure of a father;</p>
