<p class="line" name=5.3.13>Nay, godded me, indeed. Their latest refuge</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.14>Was to send him; for whose old love I have,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.15>Though I show'd sourly to him, once more offer'd</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.16>The first conditions, which they did refuse</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.17>And cannot now accept; to grace him only</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.18>That thought he could do more, a very little</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.19>I have yielded to: fresh embassies and suits,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.20>Nor from the state nor private friends, hereafter</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.21>Will I lend ear to. Ha! what shout is this?</p>
<p><i>Shout within</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.22>Shall I be tempted to infringe my vow</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.23>In the same time 'tis made? I will not.</p>
<p><i>Enter in mourning habits, VIRGILIA, VOLUMNIA, leading young MARCIUS, VALERIA, and Attendants</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.24>My wife comes foremost; then the honour'd mould</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.25>Wherein this trunk was framed, and in her hand</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.26>The grandchild to her blood. But, out, affection!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.27>All bond and privilege of nature, break!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.28>Let it be virtuous to be obstinate.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.29>What is that curt'sy worth? or those doves' eyes,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.30>Which can make gods forsworn? I melt, and am not</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.31>Of stronger earth than others. My mother bows;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.32>As if Olympus to a molehill should</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.33>In supplication nod: and my young boy</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.34>Hath an aspect of intercession, which</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.35>Great nature cries 'Deny not.' let the Volsces</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.36>Plough Rome and harrow Italy: I'll never</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.37>Be such a gosling to obey instinct, but stand,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.38>As if a man were author of himself</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.39>And knew no other kin.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>VIRGILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.40>My lord and husband!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.41>These eyes are not the same I wore in Rome.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>VIRGILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.42>The sorrow that delivers us thus changed</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.43>Makes you think so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.44>Like a dull actor now,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.45>I have forgot my part, and I am out,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.46>Even to a full disgrace. Best of my flesh,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.47>Forgive my tyranny; but do not say</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.48>For that 'Forgive our Romans.' O, a kiss</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.49>Long as my exile, sweet as my revenge!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.50>Now, by the jealous queen of heaven, that kiss</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.51>I carried from thee, dear; and my true lip</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.52>Hath virgin'd it e'er since. You gods! I prate,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.53>And the most noble mother of the world</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.54>Leave unsaluted: sink, my knee, i' the earth;</p>
<p><i>Kneels</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.55>Of thy deep duty more impression show</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.56>Than that of common sons.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.57>O, stand up blest!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.58>Whilst, with no softer cushion than the flint,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.59>I kneel before thee; and unproperly</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.60>Show duty, as mistaken all this while</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.61>Between the child and parent.</p>
<p><i>Kneels</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.62>What is this?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.63>Your knees to me? to your corrected son?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.64>Then let the pebbles on the hungry beach</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.65>Fillip the stars; then let the mutinous winds</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.66>Strike the proud cedars 'gainst the fiery sun;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.67>Murdering impossibility, to make</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.68>What cannot be, slight work.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.69>Thou art my warrior;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.70>I holp to frame thee. Do you know this lady?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.71>The noble sister of Publicola,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.72>The moon of Rome, chaste as the icicle</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.73>That's curdied by the frost from purest snow</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.74>And hangs on Dian's temple: dear Valeria!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.75>This is a poor epitome of yours,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.76>Which by the interpretation of full time</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.77>May show like all yourself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.78>The god of soldiers,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.79>With the consent of supreme Jove, inform</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.80>Thy thoughts with nobleness; that thou mayst prove</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.81>To shame unvulnerable, and stick i' the wars</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.82>Like a great sea-mark, standing every flaw,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.83>And saving those that eye thee!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.84>Your knee, sirrah.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.85>That's my brave boy!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.86>Even he, your wife, this lady, and myself,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.87>Are suitors to you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.88>I beseech you, peace:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.89>Or, if you'ld ask, remember this before:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.90>The thing I have forsworn to grant may never</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.91>Be held by you denials. Do not bid me</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.92>Dismiss my soldiers, or capitulate</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.93>Again with Rome's mechanics: tell me not</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.94>Wherein I seem unnatural: desire not</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.95>To ally my rages and revenges with</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.96>Your colder reasons.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.97>O, no more, no more!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.98>You have said you will not grant us any thing;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.99>For we have nothing else to ask, but that</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.100>Which you deny already: yet we will ask;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.101>That, if you fail in our request, the blame</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.102>May hang upon your hardness: therefore hear us.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.103>Aufidius, and you Volsces, mark; for we'll</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.104>Hear nought from Rome in private. Your request?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.105>Should we be silent and not speak, our raiment</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.106>And state of bodies would bewray what life</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.107>We have led since thy exile. Think with thyself</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.108>How more unfortunate than all living women</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.109>Are we come hither: since that thy sight,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.110>which should</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.111>Make our eyes flow with joy, hearts dance</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.112>with comforts,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.113>Constrains them weep and shake with fear and sorrow;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.114>Making the mother, wife and child to see</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.115>The son, the husband and the father tearing</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.116>His country's bowels out. And to poor we</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.117>Thine enmity's most capital: thou barr'st us</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.118>Our prayers to the gods, which is a comfort</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.119>That all but we enjoy; for how can we,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.120>Alas, how can we for our country pray.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.121>Whereto we are bound, together with thy victory,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.122>Whereto we are bound? alack, or we must lose</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.123>The country, our dear nurse, or else thy person,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.124>Our comfort in the country. We must find</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.125>An evident calamity, though we had</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.126>Our wish, which side should win: for either thou</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.127>Must, as a foreign recreant, be led</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.128>With manacles thorough our streets, or else</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.129>triumphantly tread on thy country's ruin,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.130>And bear the palm for having bravely shed</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.131>Thy wife and children's blood. For myself, son,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.132>I purpose not to wait on fortune till</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.133>These wars determine: if I cannot persuade thee</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.134>Rather to show a noble grace to both parts</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.135>Than seek the end of one, thou shalt no sooner</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.136>March to assault thy country than to tread--</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.137>Trust to't, thou shalt not--on thy mother's womb,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.138>That brought thee to this world.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>VIRGILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.139>Ay, and mine,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.140>That brought you forth this boy, to keep your name</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.141>Living to time.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>Young MARCIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.142>A' shall not tread on me;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.143>I'll run away till I am bigger, but then I'll fight.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.144>Not of a woman's tenderness to be,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.145>Requires nor child nor woman's face to see.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.146>I have sat too long.</p>
<p><i>Rising</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>VOLUMNIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.147>Nay, go not from us thus.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.148>If it were so that our request did tend</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.149>To save the Romans, thereby to destroy</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.150>The Volsces whom you serve, you might condemn us,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.151>As poisonous of your honour: no; our suit</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.152>Is that you reconcile them: while the Volsces</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.153>May say 'This mercy we have show'd;' the Romans,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.154>'This we received;' and each in either side</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.155>Give the all-hail to thee and cry 'Be blest</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.156>For making up this peace!' Thou know'st, great son,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.157>The end of war's uncertain, but this certain,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.158>That, if thou conquer Rome, the benefit</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.159>Which thou shalt thereby reap is such a name,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.160>Whose repetition will be dogg'd with curses;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.161>Whose chronicle thus writ: 'The man was noble,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.162>But with his last attempt he wiped it out;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.163>Destroy'd his country, and his name remains</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.164>To the ensuing age abhorr'd.' Speak to me, son:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.165>Thou hast affected the fine strains of honour,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.166>To imitate the graces of the gods;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.167>To tear with thunder the wide cheeks o' the air,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.168>And yet to charge thy sulphur with a bolt</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.169>That should but rive an oak. Why dost not speak?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.170>Think'st thou it honourable for a noble man</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.171>Still to remember wrongs? Daughter, speak you:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.172>He cares not for your weeping. Speak thou, boy:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.173>Perhaps thy childishness will move him more</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.174>Than can our reasons. There's no man in the world</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.175>More bound to 's mother; yet here he lets me prate</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.176>Like one i' the stocks. Thou hast never in thy life</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.177>Show'd thy dear mother any courtesy,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.178>When she, poor hen, fond of no second brood,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.179>Has cluck'd thee to the wars and safely home,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.180>Loaden with honour. Say my request's unjust,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.181>And spurn me back: but if it be not so,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.182>Thou art not honest; and the gods will plague thee,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.183>That thou restrain'st from me the duty which</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.184>To a mother's part belongs. He turns away:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.185>Down, ladies; let us shame him with our knees.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.186>To his surname Coriolanus 'longs more pride</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.187>Than pity to our prayers. Down: an end;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.188>This is the last: so we will home to Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.189>And die among our neighbours. Nay, behold 's:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.190>This boy, that cannot tell what he would have</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.191>But kneels and holds up bands for fellowship,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.192>Does reason our petition with more strength</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.193>Than thou hast to deny 't. Come, let us go:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.194>This fellow had a Volscian to his mother;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.195>His wife is in Corioli and his child</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.196>Like him by chance. Yet give us our dispatch:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.197>I am hush'd until our city be a-fire,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.198>And then I'll speak a little.</p>
<p><i>He holds her by the hand, silent</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.199>O mother, mother!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.200>What have you done? Behold, the heavens do ope,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.201>The gods look down, and this unnatural scene</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.202>They laugh at. O my mother, mother! O!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.203>You have won a happy victory to Rome;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.204>But, for your son,--believe it, O, believe it,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.205>Most dangerously you have with him prevail'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.206>If not most mortal to him. But, let it come.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.207>Aufidius, though I cannot make true wars,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.208>I'll frame convenient peace. Now, good Aufidius,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.209>Were you in my stead, would you have heard</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.210>A mother less? or granted less, Aufidius?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.211>I was moved withal.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.212>I dare be sworn you were:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.213>And, sir, it is no little thing to make</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.214>Mine eyes to sweat compassion. But, good sir,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.215>What peace you'll make, advise me: for my part,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.216>I'll not to Rome, I'll back with you; and pray you,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.217>Stand to me in this cause. O mother! wife!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.218>[Aside]  I am glad thou hast set thy mercy and</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.219>thy honour</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.220>At difference in thee: out of that I'll work</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.221>Myself a former fortune.</p>
<p><i>The Ladies make signs to CORIOLANUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.3.222>Ay, by and by;</p>
<p><i>To VOLUMNIA, VIRGILIA,  & c</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.223>But we will drink together; and you shall bear</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.224>A better witness back than words, which we,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.225>On like conditions, will have counter-seal'd.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.226>Come, enter with us. Ladies, you deserve</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.227>To have a temple built you: all the swords</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.228>In Italy, and her confederate arms,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.3.229>Could not have made this peace.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE IV. Rome. A public place.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter MENENIUS and SICINIUS</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.1>See you yond coign o' the Capitol, yond</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.2>corner-stone?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.3>Why, what of that?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.4>If it be possible for you to displace it with your</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.5>little finger, there is some hope the ladies of</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.6>Rome, especially his mother, may prevail with him.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.7>But I say there is no hope in't: our throats are</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.8>sentenced and stay upon execution.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.9>Is't possible that so short a time can alter the</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.10>condition of a man!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.11>There is differency between a grub and a butterfly;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.12>yet your butterfly was a grub. This Marcius is grown</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.13>from man to dragon: he has wings; he's more than a</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.14>creeping thing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.15>He loved his mother dearly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.16>So did he me: and he no more remembers his mother</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.17>now than an eight-year-old horse. The tartness</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.18>of his face sours ripe grapes: when he walks, he</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.19>moves like an engine, and the ground shrinks before</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.20>his treading: he is able to pierce a corslet with</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.21>his eye; talks like a knell, and his hum is a</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.22>battery. He sits in his state, as a thing made for</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.23>Alexander. What he bids be done is finished with</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.24>his bidding. He wants nothing of a god but eternity</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.25>and a heaven to throne in.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.26>Yes, mercy, if you report him truly.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.27>I paint him in the character. Mark what mercy his</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.28>mother shall bring from him: there is no more mercy</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.29>in him than there is milk in a male tiger; that</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.30>shall our poor city find: and all this is long of</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.31>you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.32>The gods be good unto us!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.33>No, in such a case the gods will not be good unto</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.34>us. When we banished him, we respected not them;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.35>and, he returning to break our necks, they respect not us.</p>
<p><i>Enter a Messenger</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.36>Sir, if you'ld save your life, fly to your house:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.37>The plebeians have got your fellow-tribune</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.38>And hale him up and down, all swearing, if</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.39>The Roman ladies bring not comfort home,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.40>They'll give him death by inches.</p>
<p><i>Enter a second Messenger</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.41>What's the news?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>Second Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.42>Good news, good news; the ladies have prevail'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.43>The Volscians are dislodged, and Marcius gone:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.44>A merrier day did never yet greet Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.45>No, not the expulsion of the Tarquins.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.46>Friend,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.47>Art thou certain this is true? is it most certain?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>Second Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.48>As certain as I know the sun is fire:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.49>Where have you lurk'd, that you make doubt of it?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.50>Ne'er through an arch so hurried the blown tide,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.51>As the recomforted through the gates. Why, hark you!</p>
<p><i>Trumpets; hautboys; drums beat; all together</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.52>The trumpets, sackbuts, psalteries and fifes,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.53>Tabours and cymbals and the shouting Romans,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.54>Make the sun dance. Hark you!</p>
<p><i>A shout within</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>MENENIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.55>This is good news:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.56>I will go meet the ladies. This Volumnia</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.57>Is worth of consuls, senators, patricians,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.58>A city full; of tribunes, such as you,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.59>A sea and land full. You have pray'd well to-day:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.60>This morning for ten thousand of your throats</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.61>I'd not have given a doit. Hark, how they joy!</p>
<p><i>Music still, with shouts</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.62>First, the gods bless you for your tidings; next,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.63>Accept my thankfulness.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>Second Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.64>Sir, we have all</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.65>Great cause to give great thanks.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.66>They are near the city?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>Second Messenger</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.67>Almost at point to enter.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>SICINIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.4.68>We will meet them,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.4.69>And help the joy.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE V. The same. A street near the gate.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter two Senators with VOLUMNIA, VIRGILIA,  VALERIA,  & c. passing over the stage, followed by Patricians and others</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>First Senator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.1>Behold our patroness, the life of Rome!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.2>Call all your tribes together, praise the gods,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.3>And make triumphant fires; strew flowers before them:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.4>Unshout the noise that banish'd Marcius,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.5>Repeal him with the welcome of his mother;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.5.6>Cry 'Welcome, ladies, welcome!'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.5.7>Welcome, ladies, Welcome!</p>
<p><i>A flourish with drums and trumpets. Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE VI. Antium. A public place.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter TULLUS AUFIDIUS, with Attendants</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.1>Go tell the lords o' the city I am here:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.2>Deliver them this paper: having read it,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.3>Bid them repair to the market place; where I,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.4>Even in theirs and in the commons' ears,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.5>Will vouch the truth of it. Him I accuse</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.6>The city ports by this hath enter'd and</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.7>Intends to appear before the people, hoping</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.8>To purge herself with words: dispatch.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt Attendants</i></p>
<p><i>Enter three or four Conspirators of AUFIDIUS' faction</i></p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.9>Most welcome!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>First Conspirator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.10>How is it with our general?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.11>Even so</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.12>As with a man by his own alms empoison'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.13>And with his charity slain.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Second Conspirator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.14>Most noble sir,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.15>If you do hold the same intent wherein</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.16>You wish'd us parties, we'll deliver you</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.17>Of your great danger.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.18>Sir, I cannot tell:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.19>We must proceed as we do find the people.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Third Conspirator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.20>The people will remain uncertain whilst</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.21>'Twixt you there's difference; but the fall of either</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.22>Makes the survivor heir of all.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.23>I know it;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.24>And my pretext to strike at him admits</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.25>A good construction. I raised him, and I pawn'd</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.26>Mine honour for his truth: who being so heighten'd,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.27>He water'd his new plants with dews of flattery,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.28>Seducing so my friends; and, to this end,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.29>He bow'd his nature, never known before</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.30>But to be rough, unswayable and free.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>Third Conspirator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.31>Sir, his stoutness</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.32>When he did stand for consul, which he lost</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.33>By lack of stooping,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.34>That I would have spoke of:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.35>Being banish'd for't, he came unto my hearth;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.36>Presented to my knife his throat: I took him;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.37>Made him joint-servant with me; gave him way</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.38>In all his own desires; nay, let him choose</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.39>Out of my files, his projects to accomplish,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.40>My best and freshest men; served his designments</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.41>In mine own person; holp to reap the fame</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.42>Which he did end all his; and took some pride</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.43>To do myself this wrong: till, at the last,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.44>I seem'd his follower, not partner, and</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.45>He waged me with his countenance, as if</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.46>I had been mercenary.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>First Conspirator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.47>So he did, my lord:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.48>The army marvell'd at it, and, in the last,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.49>When he had carried Rome and that we look'd</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.50>For no less spoil than glory,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.51>There was it:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.52>For which my sinews shall be stretch'd upon him.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.53>At a few drops of women's rheum, which are</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.54>As cheap as lies, he sold the blood and labour</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.55>Of our great action: therefore shall he die,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.56>And I'll renew me in his fall. But, hark!</p>
<p><i>Drums and trumpets sound, with great shouts of the People</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>First Conspirator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.57>Your native town you enter'd like a post,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.58>And had no welcomes home: but he returns,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.59>Splitting the air with noise.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>Second Conspirator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.60>And patient fools,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.61>Whose children he hath slain, their base throats tear</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.62>With giving him glory.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>Third Conspirator</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.63>Therefore, at your vantage,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.64>Ere he express himself, or move the people</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.65>With what he would say, let him feel your sword,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.66>Which we will second. When he lies along,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.67>After your way his tale pronounced shall bury</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.68>His reasons with his body.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.69>Say no more:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.70>Here come the lords.</p>
<p><i>Enter the Lords of the city</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>All The Lords</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.71>You are most welcome home.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.72>I have not deserved it.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.73>But, worthy lords, have you with heed perused</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.74>What I have written to you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>Lords</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.75>We have.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>First Lord</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.76>And grieve to hear't.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.77>What faults he made before the last, I think</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.78>Might have found easy fines: but there to end</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.79>Where he was to begin and give away</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.80>The benefit of our levies, answering us</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.81>With our own charge, making a treaty where</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.82>There was a yielding,--this admits no excuse.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.83>He approaches: you shall hear him.</p>
<p><i>Enter CORIOLANUS, marching with drum and colours; commoners being with him</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.84>Hail, lords! I am return'd your soldier,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.85>No more infected with my country's love</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.86>Than when I parted hence, but still subsisting</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.87>Under your great command. You are to know</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.88>That prosperously I have attempted and</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.89>With bloody passage led your wars even to</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.90>The gates of Rome. Our spoils we have brought home</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.91>Do more than counterpoise a full third part</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.92>The charges of the action. We have made peace</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.93>With no less honour to the Antiates</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.94>Than shame to the Romans: and we here deliver,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.95>Subscribed by the consuls and patricians,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.96>Together with the seal o' the senate, what</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.97>We have compounded on.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.98>Read it not, noble lords;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.99>But tell the traitor, in the high'st degree</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.100>He hath abused your powers.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.101>Traitor! how now!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.102>                  Ay, traitor, Marcius!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.103>Marcius!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.104>Ay, Marcius, Caius Marcius: dost thou think</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.105>I'll grace thee with that robbery, thy stol'n name</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.106>Coriolanus in Corioli?</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.107>You lords and heads o' the state, perfidiously</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.108>He has betray'd your business, and given up,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.109>For certain drops of salt, your city Rome,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.110>I say 'your city,' to his wife and mother;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.111>Breaking his oath and resolution like</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.112>A twist of rotten silk, never admitting</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.113>Counsel o' the war, but at his nurse's tears</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.114>He whined and roar'd away your victory,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.115>That pages blush'd at him and men of heart</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.116>Look'd wondering each at other.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.117>Hear'st thou, Mars?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.118>Name not the god, thou boy of tears!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.119>Ha!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.120>No more.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.121>Measureless liar, thou hast made my heart</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.122>Too great for what contains it. Boy! O slave!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.123>Pardon me, lords, 'tis the first time that ever</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.124>I was forced to scold. Your judgments, my grave lords,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.125>Must give this cur the lie: and his own notion--</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.126>Who wears my stripes impress'd upon him; that</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.127>Must bear my beating to his grave--shall join</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.128>To thrust the lie unto him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>First Lord</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.129>Peace, both, and hear me speak.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.130>Cut me to pieces, Volsces; men and lads,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.131>Stain all your edges on me. Boy! false hound!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.132>If you have writ your annals true, 'tis there,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.133>That, like an eagle in a dove-cote, I</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.134>Flutter'd your Volscians in Corioli:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.135>Alone I did it. Boy!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.136>Why, noble lords,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.137>Will you be put in mind of his blind fortune,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.138>Which was your shame, by this unholy braggart,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.139>'Fore your own eyes and ears?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>All Conspirators</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.140>Let him die for't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>All The People</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.141>'Tear him to pieces.' 'Do it presently.' 'He kill'd</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.142>my son.' 'My daughter.' 'He killed my cousin</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.143>Marcus.' 'He killed my father.'</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>Second Lord</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.144>Peace, ho! no outrage: peace!</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.145>The man is noble and his fame folds-in</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.146>This orb o' the earth. His last offences to us</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.147>Shall have judicious hearing. Stand, Aufidius,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.148>And trouble not the peace.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>CORIOLANUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.149>O that I had him,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.150>With six Aufidiuses, or more, his tribe,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.151>To use my lawful sword!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.152>Insolent villain!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>All Conspirators</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.153>Kill, kill, kill, kill, kill him!</p>
<p><i>The Conspirators draw, and kill CORIOLANUS: AUFIDIUS stands on his body</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>Lords</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.154>Hold, hold, hold, hold!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.155>My noble masters, hear me speak.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>First Lord</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.156>O Tullus,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>Second Lord</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.157>Thou hast done a deed whereat valour will weep.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>Third Lord</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.158>Tread not upon him. Masters all, be quiet;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.159>Put up your swords.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.160>My lords, when you shall know--as in this rage,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.161>Provoked by him, you cannot--the great danger</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.162>Which this man's life did owe you, you'll rejoice</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.163>That he is thus cut off. Please it your honours</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.164>To call me to your senate, I'll deliver</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.165>Myself your loyal servant, or endure</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.166>Your heaviest censure.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>First Lord</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.167>Bear from hence his body;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.168>And mourn you for him: let him be regarded</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.169>As the most noble corse that ever herald</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.170>Did follow to his urn.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>Second Lord</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.171>His own impatience</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.172>Takes from Aufidius a great part of blame.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.173>Let's make the best of it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>AUFIDIUS</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=5.6.174>My rage is gone;</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.175>And I am struck with sorrow. Take him up.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.176>Help, three o' the chiefest soldiers; I'll be one.</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.177>Beat thou the drum, that it speak mournfully:</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.178>Trail your steel pikes. Though in this city he</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.179>Hath widow'd and unchilded many a one,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.180>Which to this hour bewail the injury,</p>
<p class="line" name=5.6.181>Yet he shall have a noble memory. Assist.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt, bearing the body of CORIOLANUS. A dead march sounded</i></p>
